# Deferred Work

Items surfaced during code review or development that are real but not actionable in the current story scope. Each entry cites the originating story and the future story or workstream that owns the eventual fix.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-6-claude-code-pretooluse-hook-hook-check (2026-05-10)

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-COVERAGE-90PCT-2A.6** (DR1 → D2 resolution) — Story 2A.6 shipped at 86.76% repo-wide coverage versus AC12's mandate of ≥90%. Module-level coverage targets (100% on `cli/hook_check.py`, ≥95% on `claude_hooks/pre_tool_use.py`, 100% on dispatcher pre-write delta) are not demonstrated in the PR Change Log. The miss is concentrated in subprocess-fallback paths in `claude_hooks/pre_tool_use.py` (hard to unit-test) plus uncovered branches in `_resolve_path` Windows scenarios. **Owner:** focused coverage-hardening story or fold into Epic 2A retro action items; re-run `pytest --cov=src --cov-report=term-missing` and add tests until ≥90% repo + module-level targets met. Reviewer-C signoff confirmed at story 2A.6 review-C escalation.
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-TDD-COMMIT-ORDERING-2A.6** (DR2 → D2 resolution) — Story 2A.6 collapsed all implementation work into a single squash commit `1e6047a chore(2a-6): Task 11 story close-out` after 4 `git reset HEAD` operations between 20:03–20:32 on 2026-05-10. ADR-026 §1 + Story 2A.6 AC1 require TDD-first commit ordering visible in `git log --reverse` for 3 public-API surfaces (`cli/hook_check.py:main`, `claude_hooks/pre_tool_use.py:main`, dispatcher pre-write site at `_panel_helpers._run_member`). Receipts in PR Change Log narrate test-fail-then-pass evidence but reviewers cannot independently audit the ordering via git log. **Owner:** Epic 2A retrospective process action item — add a pre-commit hook or CI gate that asserts at least 3 commits exist on a story branch when public-API surfaces are touched, OR amend ADR-026 §1 to clarify acceptable receipt formats when squash is applied.

- **W1 — AC6.4 hook-load-once-at-construction not enforced** — `dispatch()` accepts `hooks: tuple[Callable, ...] = ()` per-call instead of caching at dispatcher construction time per AC6 fourth-And. Significant refactor required to constructor signature + caller wiring. **Owner:** focused dispatcher-hook-cache refactor story; open `EPIC-2A-DEBT-DISPATCHER-HOOK-CACHE`.
- **W2 — `_make_phase_gate_hook` factory pattern duplicated 3×** across `src/sdlc/cli/hook_check.py:992-1002`, `tests/integration/test_dispatcher_hook_integration.py:1411-1418`, `tests/parity/test_engine_vs_claude_hooks.py:2609-2616`. DRY violation; closure-with-marker pattern repeats. **Owner:** consolidate into `sdlc.hooks.builtin._make_phase_gate_hook(repo_root)` factory in a follow-up refactor.
- **W3 — `tests/integration/test_dispatch_disjoint_writes.py` not visibly updated despite Task 3.4 reference** — Task claims test still passes; with default `hooks=()` fixture this is trivially true (empty chain → all-allow), but does not verify the wiring path with explicit hooks injection. **Owner:** follow-up integration test extension to confirm 2A.3 fixtures pass under non-empty hooks tuple.
- **W4 — `mkdocs.yml` adds `diagnose-dispatch-failure.md` to nav (scope creep)** — Task 10.9 bundled this pre-existing strict-mode warning fix into 2A.6. Not in spec scope; acceptable but should be noted. **Owner:** next story's Change Log addendum (one-line note).
- **W5 — `pyproject.toml` uses `[tool.hatch.build.targets.wheel.force-include]` instead of canonical `package-data`** — `test_wheel_includes_claude_hooks.py` confirms wheel ships file (functional pass); spec AC8 wording prefers "package_data". **Owner:** follow-up packaging hygiene PR.
- **W6 — Latency budget magic numbers duplicated** (`_CHAIN_BUDGET_MS=500`, `_FAST_PATH_BUDGET_MS=50` in `tests/parity/test_hook_check_latency.py:2750-2751`) — DRY: spec budget change requires updating multiple sites. **Owner:** follow-up shared-config refactor extracting budgets to `tests/parity/_budgets.py` or similar.
- **W7 — Hardcoded test paths `Path(__file__).parent.parent.parent`** in `tests/parity/test_engine_vs_claude_hooks.py:2630-2632` and `test_hook_check_latency.py:2741-2743`. Brittle if test layout moves. **Owner:** follow-up — resolve `_PRE_TOOL_USE` via `importlib.util.find_spec("sdlc.claude_hooks.pre_tool_use").origin`.
- **W8 — `_emit_hook_rejected` payload omits `target_path` + `reason`** (originally F20 in code review). Adding the fields would push `_panel_helpers.py` past the 400-LOC cap (NFR-MAINT-3). Operators must currently cross-reference the paired `hook_rejected` row from `hooks.runner` to recover the deny reason. **Owner:** follow-up that either splits `_panel_helpers.py` (e.g., extract `_journal_helpers.py`) or rationalises journal payload schemas to share fields between `dispatch_attempt` and `hook_rejected`.
- **W9 — `cli/hook_check.py` cannot append to journal on Windows or fresh workspaces** (originally F4 in code review). `sdlc.journal.append` is POSIX-only (Architecture §573 — `fcntl`/`O_APPEND` atomicity), and the file does not exist before `sdlc init`. AC2.5 mandate "engine-side journal IS appended" therefore degrades to "appended when journal file exists and runtime is POSIX". **Owner:** Epic 2B — Windows-safe journal primitive (likely a per-process append-lock with explicit fsync) lifts this constraint; until then `sdlc trace --kind=hook_rejected` may miss Claude-side entries on Windows.
- **W10 — Cross-platform Windows-separator parity row** (originally F8 in code review). AC5 mandates a "Windows-style separators round-trip via PurePosixPath" path-axis case but a YAML fixture row using literal backslashes is not portable: on POSIX the backslash is a literal filename character, on Windows it is a separator. **Owner:** infrastructure work to add an `os_marker: windows` field to `tests/parity/fixtures/hook_parity_v1.yaml` plus matching skip/parametrize logic in `test_engine_vs_claude_hooks.py`. Add a unit test in `tests/unit/claude_hooks/test_pre_tool_use.py` that directly exercises `_resolve_path("a\\b\\c.md", cwd)` under `sys.platform == "win32"` until the parity infra lands.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-7-recovery-signoff-state-machine-hash-drift-validation (2026-05-10)

- **W1 — Post-approval phase-1 artifact tampering undetected** — `compute_state` only reads the canonical record; it never re-validates on-disk hashes. After APPROVED, any phase-1 artifact mutation is silently permitted; the audit-grade chain-of-custody promise (PRD §344) is broken at this boundary. Out of v1 scope per spec. **Owner:** v1.x hardening story or Epic 2B/3 follow-up — add a "verify-on-read" mode invoked by `sdlc scan`/dashboard that re-hashes artifacts against the canonical record and surfaces drift.
- **W2 — AC1 step 3 vs AC2 fifth-And spec contradiction** — AC1 step 3 says `DRAFTED_NOT_APPROVED` is for `approved: false`; AC2 + impl returns `DRAFTED_NOT_APPROVED` even for `approved: true` until `validate_signoff + write_record` runs. **Owner:** Epic 2A retrospective spec amendment to AC1.
- **W3 — Cross-phase determinism mixed with first-drift determinism** — `validate_signoff` iterates draft.artifacts in insertion order for cross-phase rejection but path-sorted order for hash drift. Mixed deterministic semantics. **Owner:** future spec/impl alignment pass.
- **W4 — Test fixture `_write_approved_record(phase=2)` with no phase-1** — `tests/integration/test_signoff_replan_invalidation.py` writes phase-2 canonical without first writing phase-1; impossible state in real workflow. Verifies the phase-3 deny logic correctly but bypasses lifecycle ordering. **Owner:** Story 2A.12 e2e suite.
- **W5 — Runbook drift after P1 lands** — `docs/runbooks/diagnose-hook-rejection.md:799` ("reader raised: ...") today maps only to corrupt canonical record; once P1 is applied (corrupt drafts re-raise), runbook needs an additional row. **Owner:** patch alongside P1.
- **W6 — Broken-symlink kind sentinel** — `compute_artifact_hash` returns `""` sentinel for broken symlinks indistinguishably from missing files. Different operational signal collapsed into same `kind="missing"` SignoffError. **Owner:** future hasher refinement.
- **W7 — Symlink loop error doesn't include cycle path** — `compute_artifact_hash` re-raises `OSError(ELOOP)` as `SignoffError` but doesn't populate `details["cause"] = "symlink_loop"` or the cycle path. Operator UX gap.
- **W8 — Symlink TOCTOU between cross-phase string check and `compute_artifact_hash`** — Mitigated by hash-via-target-bytes; defense-in-depth gap remains.
- **W9 — Path-sort case sensitivity** — `validate_signoff` uses default Python codepoint sort (case-sensitive); behavior on case-insensitive filesystems (Windows, macOS-default) under mixed-case paths is undocumented. **Owner:** Story 3.x adopt-mode hardening.
- **W10 — `compute_state(repo_root=...)` does not validate `repo_root.exists()` / `is_dir()`** — Typo'd repo_root silently returns AWAITING; phase_gate will deny for the wrong reason.
- **W11 — `_write_bytes_to_disk` uses deterministic `.tmp` suffix** — Two concurrent writers clobber each other's tmp files. Paired with D3 atomic-write decision; resolution may obviate this entry.
- **W12 — `_normalize_yaml_data` does not handle PyYAML `set`/`frozenset`/complex types** — Confusing Pydantic ValidationError on edge YAML.
- **W13 — `read_record` OSError distinction lost** — `details["cause"]` not populated; PermissionError vs FileNotFoundError TOCTOU collapsed.
- **W14 — `compute_signoff_record_hash(record: object)` duck-typed** — Should type as `SignoffRecord` via `TYPE_CHECKING` import; current `# type: ignore[attr-defined]` is unjustified.
- **W15 — `SignoffRecord.invalidated_reason` no length cap** — Malicious YAML could store arbitrary-length strings.
- **W16 — 0-byte artifact accepted** — Produces well-known empty SHA-256; passes signoff. Acceptable semantic but worth documenting.
- **W17 — `ValidatedSignoff.drift` field is forward-compat dead code** — Hardcoded to `()`; document as reserved or remove.
- **W18 — Anti-tautology receipt #1 cross-reference inconsistency** — Change Log cites property test; commit message cites unit tests. Receipt is otherwise present and gate satisfied; record-keeping issue.
- **W19 — TDD-first commit `8a6d93a` is "RED+GREEN combined"** — ADR-026 §1 wants visible RED-then-GREEN ordering in `git log --reverse`. Soft visibility violation; raise as systemic issue in retro.
- **W20 — `invalidate_record` re-invalidating overwrites silently** — No idempotency check; second invalidation loses original timestamps + reasons. Edge case for replan-then-replan flows.
- **W21 — `_phase3_warned` is process-global, not per-repo_root** — In a long-running daemon, only the first repo to encounter phase-3 emits the WARN.

Two concurrent `/sdlc-research` invocations with the same topic may resolve to the same path in v1. **Owner:** Epic 4 or v1.x — flock on `01-Requirement/02-Research/` or journal-coordinated suffix allocation.

## Deferred from: Story 2A.3 (dispatcher-primary-parallel-synthesizer-retry — 2026-05-10)

- **EPIC-4-STOP-TRIGGER-WIRE** — `dispatcher.core._emit_stop_trigger()` writes `kind="stop_trigger_raised"` journal entries (with `epic_4_placeholder=True`) on every terminal dispatch failure. The entries are written but never consumed in Epic 2A. Epic 4 Story 4.6 is responsible for reading these entries from `journal.log` and computing the actual STOP banner state for the CLI. The `dispatcher/core.py` module docstring carries a `# TODO(epic-4)` marker pointing here. **Owner:** Epic 4 Story 4.6 — wire `iter_entries(kind="stop_trigger_raised")` into the STOP-banner resolution logic.

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-DISPATCH-E2E — RESOLVED in Story 2A.8 Task 7 (2026-05-11)** — AC11 D3 (deferred): Story 2A.3 does not ship a Tier-2 e2e pipeline scenario for the full primary→parallel→synthesizer dispatch flow. The integration tests in `tests/integration/test_dispatch_disjoint_writes.py` and the unit panel suite in `tests/unit/dispatcher/test_dispatch_panel.py` provide complete behavioral coverage of AC1–AC5 and AC9 at unit + integration level. A Tier-2 fixture scenario (`tests/e2e/pipeline/fixtures/dispatch_panel/`) would add end-to-end walking-skeleton regression protection but requires Story 2A.8's full prompt-builder and workflow YAML population to produce meaningful goldens — building it now against `_default_prompt_builder` stubs produces golden files that are immediately invalidated when 2A.8 lands. **Owner:** Story 2A.8 (full context dispatch + prompt assembly) — at that point create `tests/e2e/pipeline/fixtures/dispatch_panel/` with `commands.yaml`, a real workflow YAML, specialist .md files, and `goldens/` for `dispatch_attempt`, `artifact_written`, and `stop_trigger_raised` journal entries; register the scenario in `tests/e2e/pipeline/conftest.py`. Truly closed 2026-05-11 via D7-A: normalized goldens generated (`tests/e2e/pipeline/fixtures/dispatch_panel/goldens/journal.jsonl`); byte-stable assertion added to `test_sdlc_start_success_cli`.

## Deferred from: Story 1.21 (wire-format v1 lock ceremony — 2026-05-09)

- **Hypothesis property tests for wire-format canonicalization byte-stability** — Byte-stability of `_canonical_schema_bytes(model_cls)` across arbitrary valid inputs for all 5 wire-format contracts. Per-contract `@given` strategies are non-trivial (RFC3339 timestamps, sha256 strings, nested mappings). Story 1.21 LOC budget and per-contract strategy complexity made inline implementation disproportionate. **Owner:** dedicated property-hardening story in Epic 2A or Epic 3 — create `tests/property/test_wireformat_canonicalization.py` with 5 strategies + 5 byte-stability property tests (≤100 LOC); adapt strategy patterns from `tests/property/test_replay_invariant.py:monotonic_sequence_strategy`.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-21-gate-wire-format-v1-lock-ceremony (2026-05-09)

- **D1 — AC4.2 CI anchor steps don't exist** — Spec AC4.2 places the new CI step "AFTER `state-write-protocol-validator`, BEFORE `secret-hardcode-validator`", but those names are only pre-commit hooks; the CI lint job's actual chain is `ruff → ruff format → mypy → migration-registry-lint → [new step] → pytest`. Dev placed the step in a reasonable analog slot, so impl is acceptable. Spec wording is wrong. **Owner:** next story-creation cycle (or a one-line spec-hygiene PR amending AC4.2 anchors).
- **D2 — Integration-test stdout regex fragility** — `tests/integration/test_wireformat_lock_e2e.py` asserts on stdout content (the wrap line containing "wireformat-immutability check"); a cosmetic edit to the script's print messages would silently break the test. Currently low impact because the same test also asserts exit code 0. **Owner:** future test-hardening pass — switch to a stable machine-readable marker line or assert exit code only.
- **D3 — `mkdocs --strict` collateral cleanup not in story scope** — Story 1.21 added 11 ADR nav entries (013–024) + a brand-new `Code Maps:` top-level section to `mkdocs.yml`, plus drive-by status-line edits in ADR-021/022/023 and a `docs/CODEMAPS/engine-module.md` link reformat. Necessary to satisfy AC8.7 (`mkdocs --strict` green) but not strictly within AC scope. **Owner:** Change Log addendum (one-line note that `mkdocs --strict` cleanup was bundled), OR a follow-up "mkdocs nav hygiene" PR if separation is desired.
- **D4 — Migration directory regime divergence Story 1.19 vs 1.21** — Story 1.19 ships `src/sdlc/migrations/` with a flat `v<N>.py` layout (state migrations); ADR-024 prescribes nested `src/sdlc/migrations/contracts/v<N>/<slug>.py` (per-slug subdir, contract migrations). Two parallel regimes share one package with no structural enforcement. Real risk of misplacement at first contract bump. **Owner:** the first contract-bump story (which will create `migrations/contracts/`) — add a structural test or import-time sanity check then. Document the divergence in `migrations/__init__.py` if a docstring exists there.
- **D5 — `_GOLDEN` per-fixture tests now structurally overlap snapshots** — Story 1.7's `tests/unit/contracts/test_*.py::_GOLDEN` literals lock per-fixture `model_dump(mode="json")` bytes; Story 1.21's snapshots lock `model_json_schema(mode="serialization")` bytes. Different surfaces (instance bytes vs schema bytes) but coverage now overlaps semantically. **Owner:** future test-rationalization pass once Story 2A specialist authors compose against the locked surface — decide whether to retire `_GOLDEN` literals or keep both tiers as defense-in-depth.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-18-cli-sdlc-trace-replay-logs (2026-05-09) — Chunk C (docs)

- **Schema-version emission on wire deferred to Story 1.21** (resolved Decision E1) — `_TRACE_OUTPUT_SCHEMA`/`_REPLAY_OUTPUT_SCHEMA`/`_LOGS_OUTPUT_SCHEMA = "v1"` declared in `cli/output.py:109-111` but never emitted in any JSON envelope or NDJSON line. Consumers cannot detect schema version at runtime. Decision: defer to Story 1.21's wire-format-lock ceremony rather than double-work between 1.18 and 1.21. ADR-021 update (patch C-P17) records "schema constants are internal-only until Story 1.21" as part of the 1.21 freeze contract enumeration. **Owner:** Story 1.21 (wire-format-lock).

- **Pre-flight ADR numbering contradiction in story spec** — story line 42 vs Task 8: "ADRs 015-020 in flight" vs "typically 021 if 1.17's ADR-020 has landed". Actual ADR-021 number resolved correctly. **Owner:** future spec-hygiene pass; cleanup is cosmetic.
- **Naming inconsistency across ADR-021 + CODEMAPS** — `sdlc trace` / `cli/trace.py` / `run_trace` / "trace command" / "trace tool" used interchangeably. **Owner:** future docs-style pass; create a glossary if the project ever ships external developer docs.
- **"Story 4.x" placeholder in ADR-021 line 532** (`debug_events.jsonl` ownership) — concrete story number assignable when first 4.x story is created. **Owner:** Story 4.x author.
- **`src/sdlc/cli/output.py` ~200 LOC at the cap** — Story 1.17 set the cap; Story 1.18 used the entire budget. Story 1.19 cannot extend `output.py` without first refactoring or raising the cap. **Owner:** Story 1.19 budget review (or extract per-command output helpers when needed).
- **ADR-021 Alternatives drift 1 item from spec AC8.4 verbatim list** — added `sdlc audit` combined-command rejection; omitted `--follow` no-filter alternative. Substantively equivalent. **Owner:** optional spec change-log note; not load-bearing.
- **state.json exists + journal.log missing — asymmetric behavior between commands** — `trace` silently exits 0 ("no events"); `replay` emits explicit error; `logs` prints nothing. Behavior shipped consistently per command intent; documenting the asymmetry in ADR-021 is incremental. **Owner:** future docs-hardening pass.
- **Huge `agent_runs.jsonl` (>1GB) memory behavior unspecified** — `_collect_events`/`_collect_logs` materialize full list before sort; OOMs on multi-GB streams. ADR-021 lines 583-585 already reject index-based replay seek as premature ("journals are ≤ MB at v1 scale"); same scaling assumption applies. **Owner:** future scaling/perf story; revisit when journal volumes routinely exceed MB scale.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-18-cli-sdlc-trace-replay-logs (2026-05-09) — Chunk B (tests)

- **Hash-chain integrity in test fixtures** — `tests/unit/cli/test_*.py` `_make_entry` helpers hardcode `before_hash="sha256:" + "0"*64` regardless of previous entry's `after_hash`. CLI tests verify CLI behavior; the journal hash-chain is enforced by `iter_entries` invariants tested in `tests/property/test_journal_append_only.py` (Story 1.11). Adding real chain to CLI tests duplicates the property test suite. **Owner:** Story 1.11 property tests (already exists); revisit if CLI ever validates chain integrity directly.
- **Replay `--json` missing-journal envelope shape not specifically tested** — generic error envelope shape is covered by `test_emit_error_new_codes_map_to_exit_codes`; missing-journal already routes through ERR_USER_INPUT which IS envelope-tested. Path-specific assertion is incremental, low ROI. **Owner:** future test-hardening pass when wire-format-lock (Story 1.21) freezes envelope contract.
- **AC4.2 outcome color semantics (`success`=green / `failure`=red / `partial`=yellow) not tested** — rich styling deferred per D3 decision (Chunk A v1.18 plain-text); test cannot exist for behavior that doesn't ship. **Owner:** Story 1.18.1 (rich-styling pass) along with the D3 ADR-021 update.
- **Coverage CI gate (`pytest --cov-fail-under=90`) not asserted in test code** — CI gate is config not test code (lives in `.github/workflows/*` or `pyproject.toml`). Verify in Chunk C docs/config review. **Owner:** Chunk C of this review run.
- **`pytest.mark.skipif(sys.platform == "win32")` wholesale-skips follow-mode tests on Windows** — root cause is `ctypes.PyThreadState_SetAsyncExc` flake (B-PC1) and `time.sleep` budgets (B-PC2). After those patches land the skipif can be removed. **Owner:** B-PC1/B-PC2 (Chunk B patch series).

## Deferred from: code review of 1-18-cli-sdlc-trace-replay-logs (2026-05-09) — Chunk A (source)

- **`--follow` rotation/truncation/inode-change handling NOT implemented** — `src/sdlc/cli/logs.py:233-244, 261-276`. `_poll_journal` keeps a numeric `journal_pos`. After truncate (size shrinks below `journal_pos`) the loop silently waits forever for the file to grow back past the old offset; after rotate-replace (new inode at same path) the new file's prefix is skipped entirely. Real `tail -F` handles both. Spec for v1.18 doesn't mention rotation. **Owner:** Story 1.20 (`sdlc rebuild-state`) where truncate/rebuild semantics is formalized — at that point switch `journal_pos` to `(inode, size)` via `os.stat`, reset to 0 on inode change or size shrink, and emit a warning. (Resolved as defer per Decision D2 in this review.)
- **Rich styling for human-readable trace/replay/logs output NOT implemented** — `src/sdlc/cli/trace.py`, `replay.py`, `logs.py`. ACs 1.8/3.5/4.2 declare rich-styled output via `make_console(ctx)` (bold kind name, dim hashes, rule separators, color outcomes); code ships plain text. `make_console` not imported in any of the three modules; `_OUTCOME_STYLES` constant prescribed at spec lines 859-862 silently dropped. Spec dev-note line 938 explicitly self-permits this deferral ("v1.18 ships the plain-text format"). **Owner:** Story 1.18.1 (rich-styling pass) once ADR-021 is updated to formally record the v1.18 plain-text decision and the v1.18.1 styling scope. (Resolved as defer per Decision D3 in this review; ADR-021 update tracked under Chunk C.)
- **Replay walks entire journal for out-of-range single-line lookup** — `src/sdlc/cli/replay.py:104-117`. `replay 5` correctly fast-paths via `lineno >= end and len(collected) == (end-start+1)` break, but `replay 99999999` against a small journal full-scans before emitting `ERR_USER_INPUT`. Optimization opportunity (file-size heuristic or stop-hint into `iter_entries`); not a correctness bug. **Owner:** future perf pass on the journal reader, or Story 1.20 (`sdlc rebuild-state`) which already needs file-size awareness.
- **Replay regex rejects `0` and `1-0` with `invalid_shape` instead of `inverted_range`** — `src/sdlc/cli/replay.py:25-26, 38-49`. Behavior is correct (rejection); the diagnostic message is less precise than the spec's enumerated rule names. Diagnostic-precision nicety only. **Owner:** UX-pass on CLI error messages OR Story 1.21 (wire-format v1 lock) when error-code mapping is finalized.
- **`parse_task_id` not applied to payload `task_id` values; raw-string equality only** — `src/sdlc/cli/trace.py`, `logs.py`. A typo'd-but-still-valid `--filter-task` returns silent zero matches rather than normalizing to a comparable form. Conservative (fail-closed); not a defect. **Owner:** future predicate-hardening when `payload.task_id` schema is locked by Story 2A's agent_dispatch journal contract.
- **DRY drift: `_event_affects_task` (trace) vs `_journal_entry_matches_filters` (logs)** — `src/sdlc/cli/trace.py:745-763` vs `src/sdlc/cli/logs.py:101-125`. Two parallel-but-divergent implementations of "does this entry pertain to a task" already drifting (e.g. trace checks `isinstance(payload_task_id, str)` defensively; logs runs `entry.payload.get("task_id")` twice). Refactor opportunity, not a current-story correctness defect. **Owner:** future refactor pass when a third caller (e.g. `sdlc auto`'s autoloop) needs the same predicate.
- **`_FOLLOW_INTERVAL_S=0.25` hardcoded; no exponential backoff when files are idle** — `src/sdlc/cli/logs.py:30`. 4 wakeups/sec × 691,200 stat calls/day. Fine on local SSD, suboptimal on NFS/sshfs. Spec mandates the 0.25s constant for v1.18. **Owner:** future telemetry/observability pass OR Epic 5 dashboard work where remote-FS compatibility surfaces.
- **Corrupted-journal partial state in `_collect_logs` / `_read_journal_range`** — `src/sdlc/journal/reader.py:53-64`, `src/sdlc/cli/logs.py:288-301`, `src/sdlc/cli/replay.py:104-117`. When `iter_entries` raises `JournalError(reader_invariant)` mid-stream, already-collected events are discarded; `replay 1-49` fails entirely instead of returning the readable prefix. Fail-stop is consistent with reader contract; "partial readable prefix" semantics requires spec input. **Owner:** spec clarification + Story 1.20 (`sdlc rebuild-state`) where corruption-recovery semantics are formalized.
- **`_journal_actor_matches_agent` hard-codes `"agent:"` actor prefix with `# kept for now; see ADR-021` admission** — `src/sdlc/cli/logs.py:97-98`. Brittle against future actor-format evolution; no follow-up tracking link. ADR-021 is referenced but no per-actor-prefix decision recorded. **Owner:** ADR-021 follow-up OR Story 2A.x when agent_dispatch entries finalize the actor naming convention.
- **`agent_runs.jsonl` zero-byte file silent — no diagnostic** — `src/sdlc/cli/_agent_runs.py`. Empty file yields no events with no warning; users wonder why filters return nothing. Minor diagnostic gap. **Owner:** UX-pass on CLI diagnostics, OR Story 2A's `agent_runs.jsonl` writer where the empty-file semantics is formalized.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-17-cli-sdlc-scan-status-accessibility-flags (2026-05-09)

- **State write succeeds, journal append fails → orphan mutation** — `src/sdlc/cli/scan.py:run_scan`. After `_write_state_to_disk` lands new state.json (with bumped `next_monotonic_seq`), if `_append_scan_journal_entry` raises `JournalError`, the state on disk has advanced one slot but the journal contains no entry for that slot. Story 1.20's projection reducer (`max(next_seq, entry.monotonic_seq+1)`) will diverge from disk state on rebuild. AC1.7 explicitly accepts journal-without-state mismatch as recoverable; the inverse (state-without-journal-entry) is unaddressed. **Owner:** Story 1.20 (`sdlc rebuild-state`) — define recovery behavior when on-disk `next_monotonic_seq` is ahead of the highest journal seq, and decide whether scan should attempt rollback or simply mark the slot as "scan-attempt-pending".
- **`cwd` outside repo_root falls back to cwd → misleading "not initialized" error** — `src/sdlc/cli/scan.py:_get_repo_root_or_cwd` and `src/sdlc/cli/status.py:_get_repo_root_or_cwd`. When `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` fails (no git, or cwd outside any git tree) AND cwd is a parent of an initialized SDLC repo, the helper returns cwd, then the existence check emits `ERR_NOT_INITIALIZED`. Behavior inherited from Story 1.16's helper; not a regression. **Owner:** future "repo discovery" hardening — walk upward looking for `.claude/state/state.json` instead of assuming `git rev-parse` is the only authority. Touches Story 1.16's `cli/init.py` helper plus the duplicates in scan/status.
- **`_now_rfc3339_utc()` produces `.000Z` for whole-second timestamps; sub-millisecond scan collisions share `ts` strings** — `src/sdlc/cli/scan.py`. The format `%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S.%fZ"[:-4] + "Z"` emits `.000Z` when `microsecond == 0` (or any `microsecond < 1000`). AC1.6 specifies millisecond precision so this is to-spec; Lamport `monotonic_seq` carries true ordering. External log-replay tools that key on `ts` would see ties. **Owner:** future telemetry/observability story OR Epic 5 dashboard work — switch to microsecond precision (`.NNNNNN` Z) at that point if downstream tools require sub-ms resolution.
- **`_read_state_portable` relies on `pydantic.ValidationError ⊂ ValueError`** — `src/sdlc/cli/scan.py:73-77` and `src/sdlc/cli/status.py:109-113`. Current `except (ValueError, TypeError)` catches `pydantic.ValidationError` because Pydantic v2 inherits from `ValueError`. Pydantic v3 roadmap may decouple this. Today's behavior is correct; forward-compat concern. **Owner:** Pydantic v3 migration story OR Story 1.21 (wire-format v1 lock) — import `pydantic.ValidationError` explicitly and add it to the except clause.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-15-engine-scanner-skeleton (2026-05-09)

- **Filename-vs-payload `id` field mismatch silently kept inconsistent** — `src/sdlc/engine/scanner.py:103-112`. Scanner keys `state.epics[...]` by `path.stem` and never compares to `payload.get("id")`; an `EPIC-alpha.json` whose body is `{"id": "EPIC-bravo"}` (rename-without-edit, copy-paste) is loaded under key `EPIC-alpha` while downstream consumers indexing by `payload["id"]` look up `EPIC-bravo`. Fits the explicit "v1 scanner is permissive; Story 1.20 owns reconciliation" stance from spec AC1.2/AC2.7. **Owner:** Story 1.20 (`sdlc rebuild-state`) — surface the divergence as a reconciliation warning.
- **Dead `IdsError` arm in `_load_artifacts_from_dir`** — `src/sdlc/engine/scanner.py:103-111`. The `try: parse_id(stem) except IdsError: raise StateError(...)` branch is structurally unreachable because `_walk_dir_sorted` already pre-filters by the same regex the parser uses. Defensive depth-illusion only; no runtime effect. **Owner:** revisit if `_walk_dir_sorted` is ever loosened to a glob — the test suite needs a `malformed_artifact`-via-id-parse-failure case at that point.
- **JSON files with duplicate top-level keys silently keep last value** — `src/sdlc/engine/scanner.py:50-64`. `json.loads` defaults to last-write-wins for duplicate keys (technically invalid per RFC 8259 but Python accepts). A hand-edited or merged artifact like `{"id": "EPIC-a", "id": "EPIC-b"}` is silently coerced to `{"id": "EPIC-b"}` with no warning. **Owner:** Story 1.20 / artifact-write hook (Story 2A.4) when stricter authoring validation lands — supply `object_pairs_hook` to detect duplicates.
- **Cross-process determinism test only proves same-FS-state-twice (no locale/case/hashseed parametrization)** — `tests/integration/test_scan_idempotent.py:49-67`. Subprocess-vs-subprocess invocation uses identical env on both runs; failures depending on `LC_ALL`, `LANG`, filesystem case-folding (`EPIC-Alpha` on APFS vs ext4), or `PYTHONHASHSEED` would slip through. Partial coverage exists from the Windows CI matrix (NTFS case-insensitive). **Owner:** future cross-platform CI hardening story — parametrize the test over locale + hashseed.
- **Foreign subdir-name skip emits INFO instead of WARN** — `src/sdlc/engine/scanner.py:130-132`. Spec AC2.5 governs file-level WARN for foreign filenames; subdir level is not specified. Implementation chose INFO for foreign subdir names (e.g. a stray dir under `05-Stories/`). Defensible interpretation but not explicitly covered. **Owner:** spec clarification — extend AC2.5 to cover subdir level OR document the INFO choice in ADR-018 once human disambiguates.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-14-behavioral-conformance-abstraction-adequacy-ci-test (2026-05-09)

- **Spec internal contradiction: AC1 narrative names the test `test_abstraction_adequacy_against_mock_runtime` (story spec line 29) but Task 3 (line 239) and AC2 (parameterized id contract `test_abstraction_adequacy_pipeline[mock_factory]`) name it `test_abstraction_adequacy_pipeline`** — dev correctly followed Task 3 / AC2 (consistent with `_RUNTIME_FACTORIES` and pytest id derivation); the AC1 narrative form is the stale variant. Not a code defect; spec hygiene. **Owner:** spec-correction follow-up; replace AC1 narrative form with Task 3's form.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-13-airuntime-abc-mock-airuntime (2026-05-09)

- **`tool_calls` shallow frozen-ness — inner dicts remain mutable on a `frozen=True` model** — `src/sdlc/runtime/abc.py:29`. Outer tuple is immutable but `result.tool_calls[0]["name"] = "x"` still works because pydantic v2's `frozen=True` does not deep-freeze tuple members. Dev notes (lines 671-696) explicitly acknowledge and accept this for v1. **Owner:** future story when architecture demands deep immutability — switch to `MappingProxyType`-wrapping like `JournalEntry._freeze_payload` (Story 1.7's `src/sdlc/contracts/journal_entry.py:48`).
- **Symlinked `fixtures_dir` or symlinked `*.yaml` files are followed without boundary check** — `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py:54-65, 113`. `Path.resolve()` follows symlinks; a `fixtures_dir` symlinked outside `tests/fixtures/mock_responses/` will silently load any YAML it points to. Not a security boundary (fixtures_dir is dev-controlled), but violates the implicit contract. **Owner:** runtime hardening pass — assert resolved path is under `tests/fixtures/mock_responses/`.
- **YAML aliases/anchors silently expand and can produce shared underlying dicts across distinct prompt_hash keys** — `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py:69`. `yaml.safe_load` expands `&base` / `<<: *base` patterns. If `_Fixture.model_validate` ever mutates the underlying dict, mutation leaks across records. Determinism tests don't catch this because both calls hit the shared object. **Owner:** runtime hardening pass — disable anchors via custom safe loader OR document that fixtures must not use them.
- **`MockAIRuntime.__init__` is non-async despite `dispatch` being `async`** — `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py:113-115`. Eager YAML I/O is synchronous; if `ClaudeAIRuntime` needs async construction the abstraction-adequacy claim weakens. ABC has no `__init__` contract. **Owner:** Story 2B-1 (`ClaudeAIRuntime`) when real-runtime construction shape is finalized.
- **`MockMissError` messages embed resolved absolute `fixtures_dir` path** — `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py:131`. CI runners vs dev hosts produce different absolute paths; `details["fixtures_dir"]` leaks into JSON envelopes if downstream serializers persist them. **Owner:** error-envelope hardening when telemetry pipeline is wired (Epic 5.x).
- **`test_validator_allows_mock_direct_import_in_cli` from spec Task 7 not implemented** — `tests/unit/test_runtime_import_via_abc_validator.py`. Spec listed this exact test name; implemented as `test_is_permissive_returns_true_for_cli` (helper-level, not behavior-level). **Owner:** Story 1.16 when `src/sdlc/cli/` actually exists; add the explicit allow-direct-import-in-cli test then.
- **macOS `Path.resolve()` `/var` → `/private/var` causes resolved paths to differ from caller-passed `tmp_path`** — `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py:113`. Latent test flakiness if any future test compares the stored `fixtures_dir` to the caller-passed value. **Owner:** test hardening if path-equality assertions are added; resolve via `Path(...).resolve(strict=False)` consistency or test-side resolve-before-compare.
- **`MockMissError` does not truncate long prompts or sanitize control chars in interpolated `workflow_step`** — `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py:129-138`. A caller-supplied `workflow_step` containing `\n`, `\x00`, or 10MB garbage dumps into the error message and `details` dict. **Owner:** error-envelope hardening pass; truncate `workflow_step` to ~256 chars and escape control chars.
- **`tests/fixtures/mock_responses/_smoke.yaml` checked-in fixture has no test consumer** — every test in `tests/unit/runtime/test_mock_dispatch.py` writes its own smoke YAML to `tmp_path`. Smoke fixture serves as documentation-by-example only. **Owner:** revisit if a future story (e.g., Story 1.14 abstraction-adequacy) consumes the on-disk fixture; otherwise consider deletion.
- **No test asserts schema parity between `_Fixture` and `AgentResult`** — `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py:24-44` vs `src/sdlc/runtime/abc.py:15-31`. Adding a field to `AgentResult` and forgetting `_Fixture` (or vice versa) silently drifts. **Owner:** Story 1.21 (wire-format lock ceremony) — add `test_fixture_and_agent_result_have_parity_fields` introspecting `model_fields` of both models.
  **Resolved by Story 1.21:** `test_fixture_and_agent_result_have_parity_fields` added to `tests/unit/runtime/test_mock.py`; asserts `frozenset(_Fixture.model_fields) == frozenset(AgentResult.model_fields)`.
- **Validator misses indirect-access pattern `from sdlc import runtime; runtime.mock.MockAIRuntime(...)`** — `scripts/check_runtime_import_via_abc.py:62-82`. AST import-time check cannot detect attribute-chain bypasses. Mitigated today by module-level `MODULE_DEPS["runtime"].forbidden_from` (which forbids the `from sdlc import runtime` form when called from engine/dispatcher). **Owner:** future static analysis hardening when a real bypass is observed; not worth speculative AST-traversal complexity now.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-12-state-projection-from-journal-replay-property-test (2026-05-08)

- **MappingProxyType precondition assertion is brittle to Story 1.7 changes** — `tests/unit/state/test_state_projection.py:1032-1034`. `assert isinstance(entry.payload, MappingProxyType)` couples the test to `JournalEntry._freeze_payload`'s validator order. Currently passes because the writer emits `MappingProxyType` payloads, but a future refactor of Story 1.7's payload-freezing strategy (e.g. switching to a custom immutable mapping or moving the freeze into the writer rather than the contract) would break this test with a confusing precondition error rather than a real failure. **Owner:** revisit if Story 1.7's `_freeze_payload` validator order changes OR if Story 2A-2 contract revisions touch payload-mutability semantics. Resolution: replace precondition assertion with a behavioral assertion (`dict(entry.payload)` produces a plain dict regardless of underlying type).
- **Windows CI blind spot: only POSIX-skipped tests exercise non-empty file-read path of `project_from_journal`** — `tests/unit/state/test_state_projection.py:test_project_from_journal_round_trip_via_append_sync` and `tests/property/test_replay_invariant.py:test_replay_invariant_holds_for_arbitrary_journal`/`test_replay_invariant_smoke`. All four file-write-then-read tests are gated on `@pytest.mark.skipif(sys.platform == "win32")` because `journal.append_sync` is POSIX-only (`fcntl + O_APPEND`). On Windows CI, only the `missing_file` and `empty_file` cases run for `project_from_journal`. Any regression in the read→validate→fold pipeline through a non-empty file is invisible on Windows. Architecture intentionally writes journals via POSIX primitives (per ADR-014); reading is cross-platform but the test fixtures aren't. **Owner:** future cross-platform CI hardening story OR Story 1.20 (`sdlc rebuild-state`) when adding Windows-friendly variants — replace `append_sync` with direct `_canonicalize_entry` + `Path.write_bytes` in the read-path tests so they run on Windows too.
- **Oracle's `JournalError` raise path in property test is dead code** — `tests/property/test_replay_invariant.py:_oracle_reduce` has a schema_version-drift `raise JournalError(...)` branch, but Property 2 (`test_unknown_schema_version_raises_journal_error`) hand-builds bad entries via `JournalEntry.model_construct(...)` and asserts directly against `_project_entries([bad_entry])` — never invoking the oracle. The oracle's raise branch is intentionally complete for documentation symmetry but currently provides no test coverage. **Owner:** revisit if Property 2 is refactored into a differential drift test (oracle vs production reducer agreeing on the raise message), OR if a future story removes the duplication by importing the oracle into a dedicated `tests/property/oracles/` module.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-11-append-only-journal-property-test (2026-05-08)

- **D3. Multi-process file-cache visibility on NFS / fuse / virtio-9p** — `src/sdlc/journal/writer.py:_read_highest_seq`. Same-process buffered read can return stale data after another process flushed an append on filesystems with split read/write caches. Framework runs on local disk per threat model; deferred for v1. **Owner:** future "remote-filesystem hardening" story OR first time the framework is run against a network FS in CI. Resolution candidates: (a) switch seq scan to `os.open + os.read` for cache coherence with `os.write`, (b) `os.fsync(os.open(parent, os.O_RDONLY))` before the read.
- **D4. NFC normalization of hash-suffix string fields** — `src/sdlc/journal/writer.py:_normalize_strings`. Currently recurses into `before_hash`/`after_hash`; pre-empted today by JournalEntry contract regex `^sha256:[0-9a-f]{64}$` (Story 1.7). If contract is ever loosened (combining marks, base64, etc.), NFC could change canonical bytes and break Story 1.12 hash-chain integrity. **Owner:** any future story that loosens hash field constraints OR Story 1.12 if it discovers hash chain sensitivity. Resolution: add `_HASH_FIELDS = {"before_hash", "after_hash"}` sentinel skip in `_normalize_strings`.
- **`append_sync` event-loop guard bypassable from worker thread** — `src/sdlc/journal/writer.py:742-754`. `asyncio.get_running_loop()` is per-thread; a sync-API call from inside `loop.run_in_executor` / `asyncio.to_thread` passes the guard silently. Same drift exists in `state.atomic.write_state_atomic_sync`. Document in writer docstring; backlog a unified fix for both modules.
- **`umask 0o077` collapses `0o644` → `0o600` on first create** — `src/sdlc/journal/writer.py:610`. Out-of-scope for v1; document the assumption in ADR-014 and revisit when audit-log group readers are needed.
- **Lock-path construction duplicated across async + sync paths (drift risk)** — `src/sdlc/journal/writer.py:730 vs 766`. Mirrors `state/atomic.py:185 vs 211`. Owner: extract `_lock_path_for(journal_path)` helper as part of LOC-overrun decision (D1).
- **`_write_bytes_to_journal` uses `bytes` slicing instead of `memoryview` — O(n²) for large entries** — `src/sdlc/journal/writer.py:625-630`. Mirrors state/atomic exactly; defer pending real perf signal.
- **`iter_after(threshold)` does full O(N) scan from byte 0** — `src/sdlc/journal/reader.py:489-496`. Story 1.12 (projection) will exercise this on big journals. Owner: optimization (offset cache / sidecar `.seq`) deferred until empirical signal from Epic 5 dashboards.
- **`EINTR` retry not implemented in `_write_bytes_to_journal`** — `src/sdlc/journal/writer.py:622-648`. Same gap in state/atomic; POSIX retry semantics deferred to a unified concurrency-pass story.
- **Reader yields half a stream then raises on seq regression — partial-consumption recovery contract unspecified** — `src/sdlc/journal/reader.py:466-477`. Owner: Story 1.20 (`sdlc rebuild-state`) will define recovery API.
- **Coverage `omit` for `journal/writer.py` masks Windows-side stub regression** — `pyproject.toml:196-200`. Owner: CI-config hardening — tie omit to per-OS `runner.os == 'Windows'` matrix step.
- **em-dash in linter stderr fails on Windows console with cp1252 encoding** — `scripts/check_no_journal_mutation.py:367`. Defer until reproducible on a real CI runner.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-9-foundation-concurrency-module (2026-05-08)

- **Same-process cross-instance double-lock on identical path causes deadlock** — `locks.py:_FileLock`. Two separate `_FileLock` instances for the same path in the same process block forever on the second `flock(LOCK_EX)` (flock is per-open-file-description, not per-process; Dev Notes are misleading on this point). P-4 (same-instance re-entry guard) covers the most likely accidental case. **Owner:** state/journal implementation stories (1.10/1.11) — add cross-instance guard to `__enter__`/`__aenter__` via `_LOCK_REGISTRY` path check if concurrent same-path access is observed; also fix the Dev Notes statement about "process-level coalescing."
- **AC7's ≥95% per-package coverage floor is unenforced in CI** — `pyproject.toml`. `src/sdlc/concurrency/locks.py` is unconditionally omitted from coverage measurement (Windows dev constraint). Tests pass on Linux CI but the 95% threshold is only verified manually. **Owner:** future test-hardening story — add Linux-CI-specific `pytest --cov=src/sdlc/concurrency/locks.py --cov-fail-under=95` step in CI (gated on `runner.os == 'Linux'`), consistent with Story 1.8 deferred coverage work.
- **`_in_flight` transiently stale after `asyncio.gather` exception** — `subprocess_pool.py:dispatch_many`. When one coroutine raises, `asyncio.gather` returns immediately but abandoned tasks decrement `_in_flight` only on the next event-loop cycle. Inherent asyncio limitation; no fix without replacing `gather`. **Owner:** future coroutine-lifetime hardening story or Python 3.11+ `TaskGroup` migration (allows individual task cancellation/cleanup).
- **`_in_flight` counter semantics: incremented inside semaphore block, not at acquisition time** — `subprocess_pool.py:40-46`. Cosmetic: the counter reads one lower during the window between `async with self._sem:` and `self._in_flight += 1`. No race in single-threaded asyncio. **Owner:** revisit when `current_in_flight()` is wired to a real telemetry dashboard (Story 5.x) and precision matters.
- **`asyncio.Semaphore` bound to event loop at construction — cross-loop reuse raises `RuntimeError`** — `subprocess_pool.py:26`. Creating a `BoundedDispatcher` outside an event loop and reusing it across multiple `asyncio.run()` calls is unsupported. No current call site does this. **Owner:** add a guard/lazy-init pattern if a future caller needs cross-loop reuse.
- **`_open_fd()` propagates raw `OSError` on `PermissionError` / `FileNotFoundError` instead of `DispatchError`** — `locks.py:_open_fd`. Inconsistency vs acquire helpers which wrap `OSError` into `DispatchError`. Out of AC scope. **Owner:** future `concurrency/` hardening pass — wrap `_open_fd()` in a `try/except OSError` and raise `DispatchError("cannot open lock file ...", details={"path": ..., "errno": ...})`.
- **Chaos test `proc.stdout.readline()` has no timeout** — `test_chaos_lock_holder_kill.py`. If the child crashes before printing `ACQUIRED`, the parent blocks indefinitely. CI timeout is the current backstop (acceptable for an integration test). **Owner:** next integration-test hardening pass — add `select`-based or thread-based readline timeout of ~5s.

- **`WorkflowSpec.write_globs={}` is structurally valid but semantically empty** — `src/sdlc/contracts/workflow_spec.py:24`. Required field accepts `{}`; downstream dispatcher would treat as "no agent can write anything." Validation should live at the dispatcher boundary, not the contract. **Owner:** Story 2A-3 (`dispatcher`) — add presence check for the primary_agent's write_globs entry.
- **Coverage gate discrepancy: `pyproject.toml` 90% vs AC6's 95% per-package on `contracts/`** — `pyproject.toml:129` (`--cov-fail-under=90`), `:149` (`fail_under = 90`). AC6 of Story 1.7 specifies 95% on `src/sdlc/contracts/`. Currently moot (100% achieved per file), but per-package coverage configuration would protect future regressions. **Owner:** future test-hardening story or first time per-package coverage tightening is needed; consider `[tool.coverage.report] include = "src/sdlc/contracts/*"` plus a separate per-package threshold.
- **Hypothesis is a dev dependency but no property tests for wire-format canonicalization** — `pyproject.toml:28` (`hypothesis>=6.100`). Byte-stability of `_canonicalize(model_dump(mode="json"))` across arbitrary valid inputs is a natural fit for `@given`. Today's golden-bytes tests cover one fixed input per contract; property tests would cover the full input space. **Owner:** future test-hardening story OR Story 1.21 (wire-format lock ceremony — natural moment to harden the canonicalization invariant).
  **Deferred by Story 1.21:** LOC budget and per-contract strategy complexity (RFC3339 timestamps, sha256 strings) make inline implementation disproportionate. Ownership transferred to a dedicated property-hardening story in Epic 2A or Epic 3. New deferred entry below.
- **Spec inconsistencies in Story 1.7 itself** — `_bmad-output/implementation-artifacts/1-7-foundation-five-wire-format-pydantic-contracts.md`. (a) AC1 line 33-37 lists `schema_version: int = 1` but AC2 mandates `Literal[1] = 1` — dev correctly chose Literal; (b) AC4 line 84 claims `SpecialistFrontmatter` IS hashable, AC6 line 110 contradicts itself ("Hashable: {HookPayload, SpecialistFrontmatter, ...}" then "Final hashable set: {HookPayload, SpecialistFrontmatter}"), Task 5.5 dev note corrects to `Hashable: {HookPayload}` — implementation correctly treats SpecialistFrontmatter as unhashable per Python semantics (lists are unhashable). Both are spec-doc edits, not code defects. **Owner:** Epic-1 retrospective OR next Story 1.7 spec touch — clean up AC1 wording and reconcile AC4/AC6 hashability claims.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-6-foundation-errors-and-ids-modules (2026-05-08)

- **Hypothesis `_slug` strategy capped at `max_size=5` and only generates valid slugs** — `tests/property/test_ids_roundtrip.py:18,23`. Property suite covers round-trip but never stresses long slugs (10+ segments) or shrinks toward known-bad inputs. Unit tests cover invalid cases; property suite is happy-path only. **Owner:** future test-hardening story or first regression that escapes property coverage; raise `max_size` and add `@example` for max-segment cases.
- **`parse_epic_id` fallthrough emits "slug must be lowercase kebab-case" for any non-matching `EPIC-*` input** — `src/sdlc/ids/parsers.py:77-80`. The same human-readable string is also used in `builders.py` with a different `rule` tag (`invalid_component` vs `invalid_slug`); message reuse across rule tags weakens the diagnostic. **Owner:** future Dev Notes pass or a `2a-x` story refining error-message consistency.
- **Scope leak in pyproject.toml diff** — `pyproject.toml:25-26,55`. The Story 1.6 diff includes `mkdocs>=1.6.0,<2` dev-dep addition and the `extend-exclude` widening, both of which belong to Story 1.5. Story 1.5 work was uncommitted when 1.6 began. **Owner:** developer to decide on commit splitting before pushing; if shipped together, document the conflation in the Story 1.6 commit message.
- **`SdlcError.code = "ERR_SDLC"` intentionally absent from `EXIT_CODE_MAP`, no inline comment explaining the deliberate omission** — `src/sdlc/errors/base.py:9-20`. Behavior is documented only in `test_sdlc_error_root_exit_code_defaults_to_2`. A future maintainer adding `"ERR_SDLC": 2` to the map would silently change root-class semantics. **Owner:** docstring/inline comment pass at next `errors/` revision (likely Story 1.19 migration framework or Story 2A-12 signoff).
- **`details` JSON-safety contract not enforced at error-construction site** — `src/sdlc/errors/base.py:22-25,31-38`. Type signature `dict[str, object]` accepts `datetime`/`Path`/`Decimal` but `to_envelope()` + downstream `json.dumps` will crash with `TypeError`. Per Dev Notes line 307 layering principle: redaction/serialization-safety belongs at the OUTPUT boundary, not the construction site. Narrowing the type would block legitimate nested-detail use cases. **Owner:** Story 1.8 (`config/secrets.py` + CLI `--json` writer) — adds the JSON-safe sanitization layer that wraps `to_envelope()` output before serialization.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-5-mkdocs-adr-log-skeleton (2026-05-08)

- **`license = { text = "TBD" }` first-publish guard missing from `release.yml`** — `pyproject.toml:6` (`docs/decisions/ADR-001-pyproject-metadata.md` Consequences). Proposed pre-flight: `grep -q 'text = "TBD"' pyproject.toml && { echo "::error:: license = TBD blocks PyPI publish — set SPDX identifier first (Story 1.X LICENSE-file chore)" >&2; exit 1; }` in `.github/workflows/release.yml` before the `uv publish` / `twine upload` step. **Owner:** v0.2+ LICENSE-file chore (lands the SPDX identifier; the guard becomes redundant the moment the license is set).

Proposed pre-flight: `grep -q 'example.invalid' mkdocs.yml && { echo "::error:: mkdocs.yml site_url still contains placeholder example.invalid — set real GitHub Pages URL before deploy" >&2; exit 1; }` in `.github/workflows/docs.yml` between the probe step and the `mkdocs build --strict` step (gated on `github.event_name != 'pull_request'` so PR builds still work). **Owner:** Story X.Y when GitHub Pages is enabled; guard becomes redundant once `site_url` is real.
- **Move `docs/ux/dashboard-prototype/` outside `docs_dir`** — `docs/ux/dashboard-prototype/`. - **mkdocs `1.6.0,<2` resolution against Python 3.10 floor needs CI matrix verification** — `pyproject.toml:25`. `uv lock --check` confirmed resolution holds locally (Python 3.12); CI matrix may surface different resolutions on the 3.10 floor cell. **Owner:** next CI matrix run touching docs.yml (verify in CI logs; if resolution diverges on 3.10, narrow the constraint).

- **ADR log "Status" column hides 1.5 in-place edits** — `docs/decisions/index.md:740-752`. Every row reads "Accepted" / "Accepted partial" with no indication that ADRs 002, 004, 006-010 were modified in Story 1.5 (link upgrades + Revisit-by rewrites). An auditor cannot see at a glance which ADRs were touched. **Owner:** future ADR-log-table revision (add a "Last modified by" or "Stories" column), or first index-page enhancement story.
- **Hybrid status strings on ADR-001 and ADR-005 partially overlap with index table** — `docs/decisions/ADR-001-pyproject-metadata.md:821`; `ADR-005-package-data-layout.md:903`; `docs/decisions/index.md:741,745`. ADR file status lines and index table tell partially overlapping but not equivalent stories — readers must consult both. **Owner:** schema-level cleanup at next ADR-log iteration; consider a single-source-of-truth pattern (one render generates the other).

If any later ADR accidentally references `ADR-013`, mkdocs `--strict` fails opaquely with "unrecognized link" rather than a clear "intentionally-deferred" message. **Owner:** Story 1.21 (gate: wire-format v1 lock ceremony) — the absence becomes a presence at that point, no guard needed.
  **Resolved by Story 1.21:** ADR-024 (`docs/decisions/ADR-024-wire-format-v1-lock.md`) landed; `mkdocs.yml` nav updated; forward-reference note in `docs/decisions/index.md` replaced with back-reference to ADR-024.
- **Unicode box-drawing in DAG fenced block render-dependent on browser font** — `docs/architecture-overview.md:33-44`. The ASCII DAG uses `┌`, `─`, `│`, `↓`, etc. On systems lacking the box-drawing glyphs (older Windows, some terminals exported to PDF), the diagram renders as broken squares. mkdocs `--strict` does not fail on this. **Owner:** revisit when ADR-011 permits `mkdocs-mermaid2` plugin (Revisit-by 2027-05-01) — replace ASCII with rendered Mermaid diagram.
- **`exclude_docs: ux/` may not catch non-md asset files under docs/ux/** — `mkdocs.yml:18-21`. mkdocs's `exclude_docs:` is folder-level for markdown discovery; static-asset handling for HTML/JSON/SVG under `docs/ux/dashboard-prototype/` may still be copied to `_site/`. Currently the only file under that path is `README.md` so the concern is moot. **Owner:** verify on next mkdocs build with non-md asset under `docs/ux/`; if `_site/ux/` shows up, broaden `exclude_docs` pattern to `ux/**`.
- **Hard-coded `mkdocs 1.6.1` resolved-version in ADR-011 will drift when uv.lock regenerates** — `docs/decisions/ADR-011-mkdocs-setup.md:38`. The line "Resolved version on disk: 1.6.1" becomes stale silently when uv.lock updates. mkdocs `--strict` does not fail on this. **Owner:** next ADR-011 revision — replace with `\`uv tree --package mkdocs\`` reference, or auto-derive in CI.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-1-project-bootstrap-with-uv-init-hatchling (2026-05-07)

- **`license = { text = "TBD" }` is not a valid SPDX identifier** — `pyproject.toml:6`. PyPI/twine increasingly reject non-SPDX license text. Spec Task 3.1 authorizes "TBD" as a placeholder for the substrate-only commit. **Owner:** later v0.2 chore (LICENSE file authoring).

Wheel correctly contains only `sdlc/__init__.py`, but sdist sweeps `_bmad/`, `_bmad-output/`, `.claude/`, `docs/`, `tests/`, etc. Spec Task 4.4 explicitly defers full sdist suppression (`[tool.hatch.build.targets.sdist] exclude = ["**"]`) to Story 1.3 release.yml. Patch P2 (gitignoring scratch dirs) reduces blast radius in the interim because hatchling sdist defaults to "everything not gitignored." **Owner:** Story 1.3 (CI/CD pipelines + release.yml).
- **`__version__` duplicated between `pyproject.toml` and `src/sdlc/__init__.py`** — both hardcoded as `"0.0.0"`. Future bumps will drift. Spec Task 3.3 explicitly chose static hardcoded over `importlib.metadata.version("sdlc-framework")` to keep AC2 simple. **Owner:** ADR-001 future revision (Story 1.5 authors the ADR; the runtime switch is a v1.x candidate).
- **AC1.4 literal wording vs intent** — `.python-version` AC says "declares `>=3.10`" but actual value is the pin `3.12`. Dev Notes acknowledge "the file typically holds an exact pin like 3.10 or 3.12; the constraint is enforced by `requires-python`." Spec wording could be tightened: "`.python-version` pins a Python version satisfying `>=3.10`; floor is enforced by `requires-python`." **Owner:** spec author / next epic-1 retrospective.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-10-atomic-write-protocol-chaos-tests (2026-05-08)

- **Aliased imports of `Path` bypass linter** — `scripts/check_no_direct_state_writes.py`. The AST visitor matches `Path(...).write_text` by name; aliased imports like `from pathlib import Path as P` or `import pathlib; pathlib.Path(...).write_text(...)` slip through. Acceptable today because no aliased usage exists in the codebase and pre-commit catches new ones during code review. **Owner:** the story that introduces a legitimate need to alias `Path`, OR a hardening pass when linter coverage is revisited.
- **Multi-line backslash continuation not detected** — `scripts/check_no_direct_state_writes.py`. Patterns like `Path(...) \` newline `.write_text(...)` are split across lines by ruff format anyway, and AST visit handles the chained call regardless. The gap is in source-text fallback paths. Cosmetic. **Owner:** deferrable until the AST path is replaced by a textual scan, which is unlikely.
- **NFC roundtrip property not asserted** — `tests/property/test_atomic_write_invariant.py`. State serialised with composed Unicode then re-read should normalise back to identical composed form; the current property test only verifies write→read produces the same bytes, not that decomposed inputs get NFC-normalised. ADR-013 mandates NFC at the model boundary, so this is a model-layer concern, not an atomic-writer concern. **Owner:** future hardening of `state/model.py` property tests.
- **pytest-xdist worker collision on shared `/tmp/chaos-*` dirs** — `tests/chaos/conftest.py`. When running chaos suite under `-n auto`, multiple workers may pick the same tmp prefix if `request.node.name` collides across parametrize variants. Currently fine because chaos suite runs single-worker in CI (`pytest -m chaos -p no:xdist`). **Owner:** the story that enables xdist for chaos tests.

## Deferred from: code review of 1-20-recovery-sdlc-rebuild-state (2026-05-09)

- **D1 — Concurrent `sdlc rebuild-state` TOCTOU between projection-pass and count-pass** — `src/sdlc/state/rebuild.py:64-71`. The two `iter_entries` traversals (one inside `project_from_journal`, one for the user-facing count) are unprotected by any lock; only the final `write_state_atomic_sync` acquires `state.json.lock`. Under concurrent journal writers, the success message's `entries_replayed` count may not match the actually-projected state. **Owner:** Story 1.20 follow-up (ADR-023 Concerns expansion when F13 lands) — AC2 trailing **And** explicitly accepts the no-flock design, so this is a documented limitation rather than a bug.
- **D2 — `_PROJECT_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]` hardcoded depth** — `tests/integration/test_rebuild_state_e2e.py:1115`. Pre-existing pattern shared with prior integration tests. Fragile if the test layout changes or installed-wheel CI runs are introduced. **Owner:** future test-helper consolidation story (same as prior `test_scan_idempotent.py:55-63` deferral).
- **D3 — Exact-equality dict assertion on the State model** — `tests/unit/cli/test_rebuild_state.py:1593-1595`. `assert data == {"epics": {}, "next_monotonic_seq": 0, "phase": 1, "schema_version": 1, "stories": {}, "tasks": {}}` — combined with `extra="forbid"` on `State`, any additive state-model change requires lockstep update of this assertion. Pre-existing pattern. **Owner:** revisit when the State model gains a field (Story 1.21 wire-format-v1 lock candidate).

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-0-e2e-test-harness-tier-1-cli-tier-2-pipeline (2026-05-10)

- **W1 — `--update-goldens` writes back into source-tree `scenario_dir` (non-hermetic)** — `tests/e2e/cli/test_walking_skeleton_goldens.py:644` defines `_SCENARIO_DIR = Path(__file__).parent / "fixtures" / "walking_skeleton"`; `assert_goldens` calls `goldens_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)` and `--update-goldens` writes back to source tree. By design per the spec ("authors regenerate goldens via `--update-goldens`"). Read-only CI workspace concern is covered by P1 (CI-anti-leakage assertion). **Owner:** none — accepted limitation; revisit only if golden tree migrates to a separate registry.
- **W2 — `MockAIRuntime` constructor signature / `MockMissError` message format unverified by harness** — `tests/e2e/test_harness_anti_tautology.py:1556-1567, 1581-1586` assume specific kwarg names (`fixtures_dir`) and message format (bare hex). The 9 passing tests demonstrate it works today; no current break. **Owner:** future anti-tautology hardening pass when MockAIRuntime constructor or error format is intentionally changed.
- **W3 — No positive stderr coverage in `walking_skeleton` scenario** — All three `*.stderr` goldens are empty files. Walking_skeleton CLI emits no stderr by design. Positive stderr coverage requires a distinct scenario (e.g., `error_paths`). Combined with the over-eager `_strip_uv_preamble` regex (P8), regressions in stderr could slip through. **Owner:** Story 2A.x (or a dedicated `error_paths` scenario) to add positive stderr fixtures.
- **W4 — No completeness check on per-command golden set (5 files × N commands)** — Adding a command requires 5 new goldens; orphan goldens for removed commands accumulate. No tooling validates the set. **Owner:** future test-tooling pass — add a meta-test walking `commands.yaml × command_id × {stdout,stderr,exit,journal_sha256,state_sha256}` and asserting no orphans.
- **W5 — `sprint-status.yaml` / ADR-027 status flipped in same PR as implementation** — `_bmad-output/implementation-artifacts/sprint-status.yaml:20` flipped to `review`; `docs/decisions/ADR-027-e2e-test-framework-strategy.md:42` flipped to `Accepted` in the same diff that introduces the implementation. Procedural pattern of the BMad workflow (dev → review → code-review → done). **Owner:** none — workflow design; not actionable.
- **W6 — `--update-goldens` write under xdist parallel may race** — `tests/e2e/pipeline/conftest.py:1182-1185` (and analog in `cli/conftest.py:417-418`). `mkdir(exist_ok=True)` is fine but two workers writing the same golden simultaneously is undefined. `--update-goldens` is a developer-driven action typically not run under xdist. **Owner:** document; revisit only if golden regeneration is ever parallelized.
- **W7 — `assert_goldens` extra `tmp_path` parameter (signature drift from spec AC4)** — `tests/e2e/cli/conftest.py:393-400`. Spec AC4 line 173 signature is `assert_goldens(scenario_dir, command_id, result, sdlc_dir, update)`; diff adds `tmp_path: Path` to support `_normalize_paths`. **Owner:** couples to D1's resolution — if D1 resolves by removing stdout timestamp normalization, the signature may need a re-look together with how path-normalization is plumbed.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-0-e2e-test-harness-tier-1-cli-tier-2-pipeline (2026-05-10, Round 2)

_Round 2 process-correction review (Blind Hunter + Edge Case Hunter + Acceptance Auditor) found 10 issues real but not actionable in this story._

- **WR1 — `PYTHONHASHSEED=0` in sanitized env masks hash-randomization-dependent bugs** (`tests/e2e/conftest.py:115`). No current sdlc feature relies on hash randomization for correctness. Revisit if security-sensitive code (e.g., anti-collision in token generation) is added.
- **WR2 — `_strip_uv_preamble` doesn't cover all uv 0.5+ output variations** (`tests/e2e/conftest.py:185-200`). Variations like `Built X==1.0`, `Built X (cached)`, `Built X in 1.2s` not stripped. Fix when uv version drift actually breaks goldens in CI.
- **WR3 — `_NoDuplicateKeysLoader` triple copy-paste** across `tests/e2e/cli/conftest.py`, `tests/e2e/pipeline/conftest.py`, `src/sdlc/runtime/mock.py`. Sanctioned by ADR-027 §"pytest-only goldens are sufficient". Revisit if the three copies drift and cause a bug.
- **WR4 — `mypy_path = ["src", "tests"]` widening could shadow real PyPI packages named `e2e`** (`pyproject.toml:632`). No current conflict. Defer until a real package collision exists.
- **WR5 — `mock_runtime_factory` adds no real isolation guarantee** (`tests/e2e/pipeline/conftest.py:243-268`). Premature complexity but harmless. Slides into PR7 if `request` finalizer is added.
- **WR6 — `_dispatch_panel_smoke` asymmetric error catching** (`tests/e2e/pipeline/conftest.py:187-208`). Only `MockMissError` is caught and converted to a flag; other exceptions propagate raw with no scenario context. Acceptable while only one step kind exists; reconsider when Story 2A.3 adds `cli_invoke`.
- **WR7 — AC8.4 "zero skips on Linux CI" wording fragile** — `_SKIP_NO_UV` fires on local dev boxes without uv on PATH; CI has uv installed so the binding holds. Revisit if local `make test` UX matters.
- **WR8 — `_safe_corrupt` non-ASCII coverage gap** (`tests/e2e/_anti_tautology_helpers.py:759-762`). Fallback branch's UTF-8 contract silently violated for non-printable inputs. Coverage gap; slides into PR6 if helper is ever called with non-printable goldens.
- **WR9 — Empty `01_init.stderr` golden cannot detect "stderr regression to non-empty"** (`tests/e2e/cli/fixtures/walking_skeleton/goldens/01_init.stderr`). Continuation of W3 from Round 1. Defer until a stderr-emitting scenario is added.
- **WR10 — `03_status` not separately Windows-runnable (P22 partial follow-up)** (`tests/e2e/cli/test_walking_skeleton_goldens.py`). Spec AC5.4 promised "Windows runs subset goldens (init, status non-scan) successfully"; current implementation applies `_SKIP_WIN32` at full-test level. Defer until a Windows runner is configured in CI.
