## Deferred from: full-suite quality-gate sweep (2026-05-10)

_Surfaced during a one-pass run of CONTRIBUTING.md §1 quality gate on `main` (no story attached). All other gates (ruff format/check, mypy --strict src/, mkdocs --strict, pre-commit, wire-format snapshots, coverage 91.43%) green._

- **QG1 — `test_walking_skeleton_goldens` flaky in full suite (1/4 runs failed; 5/5 in isolation)** — `tests/e2e/cli/test_walking_skeleton_goldens.py::test_walking_skeleton_goldens`. Failed once in 4 full-suite invocations on local macOS dev box; passes 5/5 when the e2e subset is run alone. Cannot reproduce in isolation → pollution from a non-e2e test in the same pytest process. Most likely culprit per WR2: `_strip_uv_preamble` regex in `tests/e2e/conftest.py:213-221` doesn't cover all uv 0.5+ output variations; some sibling test in the suite warms or invalidates uv cache state, causing the next subprocess invocation to emit an unstrip-able preamble line that leaks into a stderr/exit golden. CONTRIBUTING.md §1 floor "zero failures, zero flaky" is violated. **Owner:** future test-isolation pass — when the next reproduction lands, capture full FAILURES section (don't `tail -50` it), diff `result.stderr` against the golden, then either widen `_strip_uv_preamble` regex (per WR2) or pin uv cache via `UV_CACHE_DIR=<tmp_path>` per-test in the e2e fixture. Track concurrently with WR2.
- **QG2 — Custom in-house `# noqa:` namespaces produce 4 ruff "Invalid # noqa directive" warnings** — `src/sdlc/cli/init.py:110`, `src/sdlc/cli/scan.py:52`, `tests/integration/test_trace_replay_logs_e2e.py:78`, `scripts/check_no_hardcoded_secrets.py:33` all use `# noqa: state-write -- <reason>` or `# noqa: secret -- <reason>`. ruff's `lint.external` config option only accepts uppercase-letter-plus-digit code shapes (e.g. `["V"]` for vulture); it will not whitelist hyphenated names. Verified empirically: `external = ["state-write", "secret"]` was added to `pyproject.toml` and warnings persisted, so the change was reverted. ruff still passes ("All checks passed!") because these are warnings, not violations — but they are noise that masks legitimate ruff diagnostics. **Owner:** future tooling-hygiene story — rename the in-house namespace from `# noqa: state-write` / `# noqa: secret` to a non-`noqa` prefix (e.g. `# state-write-allow:` / `# secret-allow:`); the change touches 2 validator regexes (`scripts/check_no_direct_state_writes.py:35`, `scripts/check_no_hardcoded_secrets.py:35`) plus ~4 source callsites and ~15 validator-test fixtures (`tests/unit/test_state_write_validator.py`, `tests/unit/scripts/test_check_no_hardcoded_secrets.py`). Mechanical rename, ~20 file edits.

## Deferred from: code review of story 2a-3 (2026-05-10)

_Triaged by `bmad-code-review` (Blind Hunter / Edge Case Hunter / Acceptance Auditor); raw transcripts at worktree root `.review-*.md`. Patches and decision-needed items are tracked inline in the story file's "Review Findings" section._

- **W1 — `_default_prompt_builder` returns `specialist.body` verbatim (prompt-injection risk)** — `src/sdlc/dispatcher/core.py:95-97`. Tampered specialist.md content flows directly into the AIRuntime prompt with no sanitization. Story 2A.8 (`/sdlc-start` Phase-1 entry) is the natural owner per AC1 ("single-line scaffold returning the specialist's `body` field — Story 2A.8 will replace"). **Owner:** Story 2A.8 — replace `_default_prompt_builder` with the full prompt-shape that combines step context + sanitized specialist body + workflow metadata.
- **W2 — `_now_ts()` duplication** — `src/sdlc/dispatcher/core.py:44-46`. Inline debt comment `EPIC-2A-DEBT-SHARED-TIME` notes that `cli/_time.py:now_rfc3339_utc_ms` is the canonical source but dispatcher cannot import from `cli/` per boundary §1106. Same logic now exists in 2 places. **Owner:** future shared-utils story — extract `now_rfc3339_utc_ms` to a boundary-allowed module (e.g. `sdlc.contracts._time` or `sdlc.ids._time`) and migrate both call sites.
- **W3 — `panel_outputs` synth-context unbounded by output size** — `src/sdlc/dispatcher/core.py:354-365`. Synth's `extra_context["panel_outputs"]` collects every panel member's `output_text`. With `MockAIRuntime` outputs are tiny; with `ClaudeAIRuntime` (Epic 2B) a 10MB parallel output would land in the synth prompt context and hit token limits. **Owner:** Story 2B.1 (ClaudeAIRuntime) — add output-size cap or lazy-fetch pattern; spec the contract for "max panel-output bytes".
- **W4 — `BoundedDispatcher._in_flight` non-atomic counter** — `src/sdlc/concurrency/subprocess_pool.py:40-46`. Acceptable under single-event-loop assumption (current architecture); `current_in_flight()` accessor returns a stale snapshot the moment after read. Tests `test_panel_concurrency.py` poll this for peak-in-flight assertions and may false-pass on Windows ProactorEventLoop. **Owner:** future test-isolation story — either document the single-loop precondition explicitly in `BoundedDispatcher` docstring + assert no multi-loop usage, OR replace counter with `asyncio.Lock`-protected `_in_flight`.
- **W5 — `time.monotonic()` Windows ~15ms granularity** — `src/sdlc/dispatcher/core.py:184, 191`. `duration_ms` for sub-15ms operations rounds to 0 on Windows. Pre-existing platform limitation; affects telemetry granularity but not correctness. **Owner:** future performance-telemetry story — switch to `time.perf_counter_ns()` for higher-resolution timing.
- **W6 — `_AgentRunLine.schema_version=1` hardcoded** — `src/sdlc/telemetry/runs.py:76, 115`. Intentional per AC9 ("AgentRun is a 2A placeholder; full wire-format lock arrives in Epic 2B Story 2B.1. Format may evolve in 2A without ADR-024 ceremony."). **Owner:** Story 2B.1 — full wire-format lock + ADR-024 snapshot ceremony for `agent_runs.jsonl`.
- **W7 — `record_agent_run` no fsync** — `src/sdlc/telemetry/runs.py:90-91, 128-129`. Python text-mode `open("a")` is block-buffered; line stays in OS page cache until close. A crash between dispatch_panel completing and process exit loses telemetry. Journal does fsync; runs.jsonl does not. AC9 places `agent_runs.jsonl` outside wire-format contract scope, so durability is explicitly Epic 2B concern. **Owner:** Story 2B.1 — add fsync semantics matching `journal/writer.py` shape when telemetry becomes a wire-format contract.
- **W8 — Boundary linter dispatcher allowlist over-broad** — `scripts/check_module_boundaries.py:84-102`. `dispatcher.depends_on = {"errors", "runtime", "workflows", "specialists", "state", "journal", "hooks", "telemetry", "concurrency", "config", "contracts", "ids"}` per Architecture §1067; current `dispatcher/core.py` only imports `errors, runtime, journal, specialists, telemetry, contracts, concurrency`. The unused entries (`state, hooks, ids, workflows, config`) are reserved for future Layer-2/3 stories (2A.6 hooks, 2A.10 postconditions). Acceptable for now. **Owner:** future boundary-tightening pass when all Layer 2 stories ship — prune unused deps and revalidate.

## Deferred from: code review of story 2a-3 — patches applied (2026-05-10)

_Surfaced and applied by `bmad-code-review` patches; the items below are residuals carrying their own debt tickets._

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE** — `_run_member` writes specialist artifacts via `Path.write_text(...)` (`src/sdlc/dispatcher/_panel_helpers.py` write site). `state.atomic.write_state_raw_atomic_sync` is JSON-only + POSIX-only and does not accept arbitrary text. AC8's escape hatch documented this debt; this entry formalizes it. **Owner:** Epic 2B Story 2B.1 — port a raw-text atomic primitive (temp-file + rename + parent-fsync) usable for arbitrary specialist outputs; cross-platform. Until then the dispatcher's artifact write is non-atomic against process crash mid-write (the journal `artifact_written` entry will be missing if so, leaving disk + journal consistent on the failure side).
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-COVERAGE-PRE-EXISTING** (DR4 of Story 2A.3 review) — Repo-wide coverage 85% sits below the AC12 ≥90% gate. The depression is caused by 50 pre-existing failing tests (per Story 2A.3 Completion Notes) in modules outside 2A.3's scope (`journal/writer.py`, `state/rebuild.py`, `cli/{_hook_trust_writer,status,trust_hooks,_init_hook_baseline,scan}.py`, etc.). All NEW dispatcher/telemetry modules ship at 100% coverage. **Owner:** future test-fix sweep — fix the 50 pre-existing failures so their code paths execute under coverage. Until then, `pyproject.toml` `[tool.coverage.report].fail_under` is pinned at 85 with this debt ticket cited inline.
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-PANEL-V1-PROCESS-LOCAL-SEQ** (P1 of Story 2A.3 review) — Panel dispatch's `monotonic_seq` is allocated via a process-local async lock + cached counter in `dispatcher/_panel_helpers.py:_allocate_seq`. This is correct for v1's single-process dispatcher (per AC1) but races against any other process appending to the same `journal_path` simultaneously. The original implementation hard-coded `seq=0,1,2` per `_run_member` call, which the journal writer's `_seq._read_highest_seq` enforcement at `journal/writer.py:170-180` would reject — the bug was invisible only because tests mock `journal_append`. **Owner:** Epic 2B Story 2B.1 (alongside `ClaudeAIRuntime` which introduces real cross-process dispatch) — add a public `journal.append_with_seq_alloc(entry_factory, journal_path)` API that holds the journal flock across `_read_highest_seq` + `entry_factory(seq)` + `_append_protocol_body` to allocate seq atomically across processes. Migrate dispatcher to call it; remove `_SEQ_LOCKS`/`_SEQ_CACHE`/`_allocate_seq` private helpers.
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-JOURNAL-NULL-AFTER-HASH** (P19 partial of Story 2A.3 review) — `JournalEntry.after_hash` is a non-null sha256-pattern string (`src/sdlc/contracts/journal_entry.py:25`). For non-state-mutation journal kinds (`dispatch_attempt`, `stop_trigger_raised`) the dispatcher uses a sentinel hash `_NULL_HASH = "sha256:" + "0" * 64`, which is meaningless for events that don't mutate any artifact. Downstream replay/audit consumers may treat the sentinel as a real state hash. **Owner:** Epic 2B Story 2B.1 — relax `JournalEntry.after_hash` to `Optional[Annotated[str, ...]]` for non-mutation kinds (paired with snapshot regen ceremony per ADR-024 mutation taxonomy) OR add a `kind`-discriminated `after_hash` policy in the contract. Until then, sentinel hash documents the non-mutation semantics in code.
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-WIN32-RUNS-LOCK — reclassified 2026-05-22 (ADR-034): debt row `EPIC-2A-D7B`, severity BLOCKING→LOW, deferred** — no Windows CI runner exists (`ci.yml` matrix is ubuntu+macos) and the framework is POSIX-only in v1 (`journal/writer.py` raises on Windows); reactivate when Windows becomes a supported target. (P5 partial of Story 2A.3 review) — Windows branch of `record_agent_run` writes `agent_runs.jsonl` without `file_lock` (POSIX `fcntl.flock` is the only locking primitive currently exposed by `concurrency/locks.py`). Concurrent panel dispatch on Windows would interleave bytes — but is also gated by `journal/writer.py` being POSIX-only (raises `JournalError` on Windows), so parallel panel dispatch is unreachable on Windows in v1. Single-write production paths function correctly. **Owner:** Story 2B.1 — port `concurrency.locks.file_lock` to Windows via `msvcrt.locking()` or fall back to `portalocker`; remove the platform-branch in `telemetry/runs.py`.
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-PANEL-ORPHAN-NOTE** (P4 informational of Story 2A.3 review) — `dispatch_panel` no longer uses `BoundedDispatcher.dispatch_many` for parallel members; it uses inline `asyncio.Semaphore(max_parallel_agents)` + `gather(return_exceptions=True)` to prevent orphan coroutines on first failure (the `dispatch_many` API uses `gather(return_exceptions=False)` which leaves siblings running per Python asyncio docs). This is a deliberate spec-AC2-step-2 deviation: the throttling pattern is preserved (semaphore-bounded), but the API call is inlined for safety. **Owner:** future concurrency hardening — extend `BoundedDispatcher` with a `dispatch_many_collect()` method that returns `list[T | BaseException]` and migrate `dispatch_panel` back to it.

## Deferred from: Story 2A.4 (pre-write hook chain — naming_validator + phase_gate, 2026-05-10)

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-HOOK-CHAIN-E2E — Full hook-chain end-to-end test through CLI dispatch** — `run_hook_chain` is integration-tested via `tests/integration/test_hook_chain_smoke.py` (naming_validator → phase_gate with mocked journal), but there is no end-to-end test invoking the real CLI dispatch path that wires `HookPayload` construction → `run_hook_chain` → journal write for a phase-gated artifact write attempt. The full dispatch wiring is deferred to the dispatcher story (2A.3 or later). **Owner:** Story 2A.3 (dispatcher primary/parallel/synthesizer) when `write_artifact` CLI surface lands — add e2e test asserting that a Phase-2 write without a Phase-1 signoff exits non-zero and emits a `hook_rejected` journal entry.

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-PHASE-GATE-READ — RESOLVED in Story 2A.7 Task 6 (P3, 2026-05-10)** — `phase_gate` now consumes signoff state via a `signoff_reader: Callable[[int, Path], str]` DI parameter (Story 2A.7 AC7 + AC11/D1 D2). The direct `yaml.safe_load` reader has been removed. The dispatcher boundary owns wiring via `sdlc.dispatcher.build_pre_write_hook_chain(repo_root)` which composes `(naming_validator, phase_gate-with-signoff_reader)` for `run_hook_chain` consumption. `hooks/` does NOT import `signoff/` — boundary preserved per Architecture §1067/§1109.

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-REPLAN-INVALIDATION-WIRE — CLOSED in Story 2A.19 (2026-05-19)** — `cli/replan_cmd.py:run_replan` calls `invalidate_record` for every APPROVED phase ≥ scope_phase (AC3) and appends `kind="replan_invalidated"` + per-phase `kind="signoff_invalidated"` journal entries (AC4). The replan-then-replan guard (AC3) skips phases already `INVALIDATED_BY_REPLAN`. Item (3) (downstream dirty-flags in `state.json`) is deliberately deferred as `EPIC-2A-DEBT-REPLAN-DIRTY-PROJECTION` (see below). Opened by Story 2A.7 Task 11.5; closed by Story 2A.19 AC3 + AC4.

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-REPLAN-FINE-GRAINED-DAG — Phase-based downstream is coarse-grained; artifact-level provenance graph deferred** — `compute_downstream` (Story 2A.19) returns every file under phases numerically > scope_phase. A true artifact-provenance graph (architecture concern #16) would let `sdlc replan` scope invalidation to the specific epic/story subtree affected. v1 trades precision for simplicity. **Owner:** Epic 5 or dedicated DAG story — build a graph from epic/story JSON dependencies and wire it into `compute_downstream`.

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-REPLAN-DIRTY-PROJECTION — `state.json` does not reflect replan dirty-flags** — After `sdlc replan`, the `replan_invalidated` payload lists `downstream_artifacts`, but `sdlc scan` does not yet fold this into a `dirty_flags` field in `state.json`. The `/sdlc-next` router (2A.18) and Epic 5 dashboard rely on `state.json` for readiness checks; until the projection exists, post-replan `state.json` is stale. **Owner:** `sdlc scan` story in Epic 3 or 4 — extend `scanner.py` to read `replan_invalidated` entries from the journal and emit `dirty: true` on affected artifact states.

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-SIGNOFF-FLOCK-CONCURRENCY — RESOLVED 2026-05-22 (ADR-034, debt row `EPIC-2A-D7A`)** — `write_record`/`invalidate_record` now hold a per-phase POSIX flock (`_signoff_write_lock` at `<target>.lock`) across the exists-check/TOCTOU-read + `tmp+replace`; two behavioural tests verify the serialisation. Original report follows. Concurrent `write_record`/`invalidate_record` callers raced the `tmp+replace` pattern — `_write_bytes_to_disk` in `src/sdlc/signoff/records.py` adds `os.fsync(fd)` to make the write durable before the `os.replace` rename (Story 2A.7 D3 patch), but does NOT take a file lock. Two concurrent processes (e.g. CI fanout + a stray dev console) hitting `write_record(phase)` simultaneously can both pass the `target.exists()` guard, both create the same deterministic `phase-N.yaml.tmp` path, and the second `replace` silently wins. Cross-platform flock (POSIX `fcntl.flock` + Windows `msvcrt.locking`) is the canonical fix. **Owner:** post-Epic-2A hardening pass — adopt or extend `state.atomic.write_atomic` with a Windows-aware lock helper; replace `_write_bytes_to_disk` callers with the canonical surface. Tracked per Story 2A.7 D3 review decision.

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-BYPASS-FLAG-WIRING — `--force-bypass-signoff` CLI flag not yet wired to dispatch** — `validate_bypass_request` in `src/sdlc/cli/_bypass.py` (AC7/AC8) validates the bypass preconditions (justification ≥10 chars, trust store not uninitialized or corrupted) but the `--force-bypass-signoff` flag itself is not yet plumbed into any CLI command or dispatcher call-site. The validation helper exists and is tested, but no CLI surface calls it. **Owner:** the story that ships `sdlc write` or equivalent dispatch CLI command — add `--force-bypass-signoff` + `--justification` flags to that command, call `validate_bypass_request`, and pass `bypass_phase_gate=True, justification=justification` to `run_hook_chain`.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-8-sdlc-start-phase-1-entry (2026-05-11)

- **W1 — Non-atomic `product_path.write_text` (TOCTOU + crash window between write and journal append)** — Inherited as `EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE` per spec line 84; deferred to Story 2B.1 (`ClaudeAIRuntime` + atomic raw-text write primitive). - **W2 — `_read_highest_seq + 1` racy across CLI/dispatcher in multi-process** — D4-B resolution kept dispatcher-owned `_allocate_seq` allocator; cross-process correctness inherited as `EPIC-2A-DEBT-PANEL-V1-PROCESS-LOCAL-SEQ`. **Owner:** future multi-process safety story (no Layer-4 owner).
- **W3 — `cli/start.py` LOC overage (376 lines vs AC10 250 cap)** — After Phase 2 D2-B refactor (which moved frontmatter assembly into the synthesizer pipeline), `cli/start.py` is 376 lines, still over the AC10 250-cap. **Owner:** open follow-up debt `EPIC-2A-DEBT-CLI-START-LOC-CAP`; split helpers (e.g., `_materialize_phase1_mock_fixtures`, `PanelObserver` construction, post-dispatch verification) into helper modules.
- **W4 — `cli.depends_on` accumulating modules (dispatcher, workflows, specialists, signoff, runtime, workflows_yaml per Phase 3 fix)** — `scripts/check_module_boundaries.py` was widened multiple times across Stories 2A.6, 2A.7, 2A.8. Cumulative effect erodes ADR-010 thin-cli intent. **Owner:** follow-up ADR proposal to either ratify cli's expanded surface OR introduce an `engine` intermediary.
- **W5 — Real prompt-injection adversarial corpus (NFR-SEC-3 behavioral verification)** — Phase 1 hardening covers structural defenses (boundary block tags + Unicode normalization + envelope-fragment rejection + length cap + control-char strip); behavioral verification against a real adversarial corpus remains Epic 2B scope. **Owner:** Epic 2B specialist authoring + prompt-injection corpus.
- **W6 — `agent_runs.jsonl` partial-state pollution after panel failure** — Failed panels leave `dispatch_prompt` rows for primary/parallel members, polluting the `boundary_line_present_in_prompts` postcondition on the next run. **Owner:** new debt for failed-run telemetry cleanup; coordinate with retry-policy / replan story.
- **W7 — Atomic raw-text write primitive (`write_artifact_atomic_sync` for non-JSON)** — Inherited per spec line 84. **Owner:** Story 2B.1.
- **W8 — `_check_product_md_exists` `split('---', 2)` body-with-HR ambiguity** — Use a proper frontmatter parser (e.g., `python-frontmatter` or anchored regex). **Owner:** follow-up postconditions hardening or formal frontmatter parser introduction.
- **W9 — `dispatch_panel` parameter explosion (resolved by D1-C)** — D1-C resolution introduced `PanelObserver` injection object; the `cli_*` kwargs are removed. Entry kept as historical reference; CLOSED by Phase 2 refactor.
- **W10 — Phase-1 fail-mid-dispatch journal orphans** — `agent_dispatched` entries written for primary/parallel before a sibling fails leave the journal with no paired `artifact_written` or `panel_aborted`. Recovery semantics need a new journal kind (`panel_aborted`). **Owner:** coordinate with Story 2A.19 (`sdlc replan`) — depends on `JournalEntry.kind` extensibility posture.
- **W11 — Hardcoded `_PRODUCT_REL`, `_JOURNAL_REL`, `_RUNS_REL` paths (drift bait)** — Module-level constants in `cli/start.py` duplicate knowledge across `phase_gate`, `scan`, `status`. **Owner:** future central path-registry refactor (e.g., `src/sdlc/paths.py`).
- **W12 — `idea_hash` threat-model documentation** — Spec line 97 says `idea_hash` is for audit-trail correlation, not security. Brute-force recoverable for low-entropy ideas. **Owner:** Epic 2B security threat-model docs.
- **W13 — `pyproject.toml` mypy 3.10→3.12 bump consistency vs `requires-python`** — Verify `[project].requires-python = ">=3.12"` was updated outside this diff. **Owner:** packaging audit — verify externally, file follow-up if requires-python is not pinned.
- **W14 — `signoff/records.py` LOC exemption from `check_module_boundaries.py:_is_loc_exempt`** — File-by-name exemption was added during Story 2A.7. **Owner:** follow-up refactor story.
- **W15 — `dispatcher/_panel_helpers.py` LOC exemption (543 LOC; LOC-exempt)** — Story 2A.8 Phase 2 refactor added complexity; planned split is W17 below. **Owner:** Story 2A.8 follow-up — remove exemption after W17 split lands.
- **W16 — `dispatch_panel`'s `_is_phase1_prompt_builder` introspection** — Phase 2 introduced `_is_phase1_prompt_builder` (signature-based dispatch between legacy 2-arg and Phase-1 kw-arg builders) to keep both `dispatch()` and `dispatch_panel()` working through a single `prompt_builder` parameter. This is fragile under future builder protocol changes. **Owner:** when Story 2A.13/2A.14 retires `_legacy_default_prompt_builder`, also retire `_is_phase1_prompt_builder` and converge on the Phase-1 signature.
- **W17 — Split `_run_member` into private helpers (P45 deferred)** — `_emit_agent_dispatched_entry`, `_record_artifact_run` seams already exist; current `noqa: C901, PLR0915` debt acknowledged. Phase 2 D1-C refactor added the `PanelObserver` plumbing through `_run_member`, increasing branching. **Owner:** focused refactor follow-up — split into helpers and remove the `noqa` markers + W15 LOC exemption.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-9-sdlc-research (2026-05-11)

- **W1 — Tail state-update failure leaves `state.next_monotonic_seq` stale vs journal** (originally E3 in code review) — After `_research_dispatch_async` commits the `artifact_written` journal entry, any failure in the outer state read/atomic-write tail (OSError, StateError, file deleted mid-run) leaves the artifact + journal entry persisted but `state.next_monotonic_seq` un-bumped. Next allocator reads journal max+1 so seq is fine in-flight, but the state.json invariant "authoritative seq counter" is silently lied to. Same posture as `cli/start.py:run_start`. **Owner:** open `EPIC-2A-DEBT-RESEARCH-STATE-TAIL-DIVERGENCE`; either (a) emit state.next_monotonic_seq update INSIDE the flocked journal append region (cross-process atomicity), or (b) document the partial-failure window in research.py module docstring and add a recovery hint when the state.json bump fails.
- **W2 — `target_path.write_text` non-atomic vs `after_hash` commitment** (originally E10+F21 in code review) — Direct `Path.write_text` is non-atomic; on torn write the file is half-written, but the journal's `after_hash` is computed against the in-memory `final_text`. Audit-log lie at the byte level: `sdlc replay --verify-hashes` finds drift. Same author imports atomic-write primitives for state and chose not to use one for the artifact. **Owner:** re-cites `EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE` — Story 2B.1 atomic raw-text write primitive resolves this for the whole codebase.
- **W3 — Same-process intra-thread dedup-suffix race** (originally E4+F5 in code review) — Module docstring acknowledges cross-process race, but two concurrent `asyncio` tasks within the same process — or any future intra-process parallel invocations from a single CLI session — share no in-memory lock either. Acknowledging cross-process debt does not cover same-process safety. **Owner:** broaden `EPIC-2A-DEBT-RESEARCH-DEDUP-RACE` scope to cover intra-process; tighten via `O_CREAT|O_EXCL` reservation right after path resolution, OR flock-on-research-dir bracketing both `_next_research_path` and `target_path.write_text`.
- **W4 — `phase_gate`-without-`__is_phase_gate__`-marker test coverage lost** (originally F15 in code review) — The deleted `_make_phase_gate_hook_direct` helper specifically created a phase_gate closure WITHOUT the `__is_phase_gate__` attribute to exercise the runner's bypass semantics on un-marked hooks. Replacing all call sites with `build_pre_write_hook_chain(tmp_path)` means every direct test now uses chain-built phase_gate which carries the marker. Marker-missing path is implicitly untested. **Owner:** hook-runner test-suite hardening pass — keep at least one no-marker construction site, OR document that the marker is now a hard contract (no un-marked phase_gate allowed).
- **W5 — `research_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)` runs before all preflight branches resolve** (originally F11 in code review) — Phase check happens before mkdir but preflight ordering creates `01-Requirement/02-Research/` even when later operations refuse. Works under current `emit_error`-raises semantics; fragile if `emit_error` ever returns. **Owner:** defer until `emit_error` is refactored or until the ordering becomes a real concern.
- **W6 — Golden journal fixture freezes `dispatch_attempt` coupling** (originally F13 in code review) — Golden expects `agent_dispatched` + `dispatch_attempt` + `artifact_written`. Dispatcher refactor that suppresses `dispatch_attempt` on `persist_artifact=False` (or rationalises payload schemas) breaks this test for an unrelated reason. **Owner:** consolidation pass on dispatcher journal payload schemas.
- **W7 — Non-numeric-suffix files silently ignored by dedup** (originally E5 in code review) — User manually placing `pci-scope-draft.md` is invisible to `_occupied_research_suffixes`. Operators expect "preserve all prior research" — dedup counter and audit miss the draft. **Owner:** defensive future warning — echo to stderr when non-numeric-suffix files match the slug prefix, OR filter the glob to `[0-9]+` suffix.
- **W8 — Fixture-write `OSError` mis-classified as dispatch failure** (originally E8 in code review) — `_materialize_research_mock_fixtures` write inside `tempfile.TemporaryDirectory()` raises bare `OSError` on disk-full; caught by broad `except Exception` and emitted as `ERR_RESEARCH_DISPATCH_FAILED`. Misleading provenance. Same defect in `cli/start.py`. **Owner:** cross-cutting fix — wrap fixture materialization separately and emit `ERR_INFRASTRUCTURE`.
- **W9 — Symlink TOCTOU between dispatcher write and outer relative_to resolve** (originally E11 in code review) — Between `_research_dispatch_async`'s `write_text` (line 254) and outer `target_path.resolve().relative_to(root.resolve())` (line 444), someone replacing `01-Requirement/02-Research` with a symlink causes `ValueError` AFTER artifact + journal committed. Very unlikely in production. **Owner:** structured return type from `_research_dispatch_async` carrying `rel_art` resolves this once P20 lands.
- **W10 — `read_state_or_refuse` returning None message conflates initial-state-missing vs TOCTOU deletion** (originally E12 in code review) — Line 309 emits "no .claude/state/state.json found; run 'sdlc init' first" for both first-run-on-empty-repo and concurrent-deletion-mid-run. Inconsistent with line 425-429 which uses "state.json disappeared mid-run". **Owner:** low-impact diagnostic clarity fix.
- **W11 — `agent_dispatched` emitted BEFORE pre-write hooks (overpromises on hook denial)** (originally E19 in code review) — `_panel_helpers._run_member` emits `agent_dispatched` at line 402, runs `_run_pre_write_hooks` at line 447, then runtime.dispatch at line 460. If hooks deny, journal records "agent dispatched" for a target whose write was never actually offered. Audit reconstructions lie. Cross-story: affects `start.py` panel path too. **Owner:** reorder emit to AFTER hook chain runs — coordinate with Story 2A.4 owner since this changes the dispatcher contract.
- **W12 — `_slugify_topic` unreachable defensive branches** (originally F3 in code review) — Lines 83-89 contain dead branches given the regex contract that slugs never start with `-` and parts are always non-empty. Algorithm works; defensive code is unreachable. **Owner:** cleanup pass — simplify and document the invariant; replace unreachable `else` with `raise WorkflowError("internal: slug truncation produced empty result")` so future invariant breaks are loud.
- **W13 — `pkg.__file__` may be None for namespace packages / zipapps** (originally F23 in code review) — `_workflows_package_dir()` uses `Path(pkg.__file__).resolve().parent`; raises `TypeError` if `sdlc.workflows_yaml` ever becomes a namespace package or is zipapp'd. **Owner:** swap to `importlib.resources.files(pkg)` in a future packaging-hygiene pass.

### D-decision-derived debts (opened during review-A 2026-05-11)

- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-TDD-COMMIT-ORDERING-2A.9** (D2 resolution) — Story 2A.9 was implemented entirely in the worktree (no commits on `story/2a-9-sdlc-research` branch versus `main@32096b0`). ADR-026 §1 + spec line 300 require TDD-first commit ordering visible in `git log --reverse` for the 5 public-API surfaces (AC1, AC3, AC5, AC6, AC11). Receipts in Change Log narrate "test-fail-then-pass per task" but reviewers cannot independently audit ordering via git log. **Match precedent:** Story 2A.6 DR2 → D2 resolution. **Owner:** Epic 2A retrospective process action — pre-commit hook or CI gate asserting ≥ N commits on a story branch when public-API surfaces are touched, OR amend ADR-026 §1 to clarify acceptable receipt formats when squash is applied.
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-CLI-RESEARCH-LOC-CAP** (D3 resolution) — `src/sdlc/cli/research.py` is 458 LOC versus AC10 cap of 350 LOC. Dev added the file to the LOC exempt list in `scripts/check_module_boundaries.py` rather than splitting. **Match precedent:** Story 2A.8 W3 (`cli/start.py` 376 LOC vs 250 cap, opened `EPIC-2A-DEBT-CLI-START-LOC-CAP`). **Owner:** follow-up focused refactor story — extract `_research_dispatch_async` + `_materialize_research_mock_fixtures` + journal/state-update tail into helper modules. Consider folding with `cli/start.py` split — both have similar materialize-fixtures + post-dispatch verification shape.
- **EPIC-2A-DEBT-RESEARCH-MOCK-GATE** (P18 from code review, deferred to v1.x) — `sdlc research` currently writes a `**PLACEHOLDER**`-marked mock body and emits a stderr `[WARN]` block; strict `--allow-mock` gating (refuse to run without explicit acknowledgment) is deferred until Story 2B.1 (`ClaudeAIRuntime`) makes real dispatch the default. Until then the strong warning + body marker is the user-education mechanism. **Owner:** Story 2B.1 — at the same time as ClaudeAIRuntime lands, flip the default; existing tests will require `--allow-mock` argument propagation.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-13-sdlc-ux-phase-2-ux-track (2026-05-14)

Used in the `agent_dispatched` journal entry's `target_id` but the file is never written (`persist_artifact=False`). Result: Phase 2 UX writes ship without an explicit prompt-injection-boundary gate in v1. **Owner:** Security review / Story 2B.9 maintainer. **Activation trigger:** real runtime lands OR a Phase-2 specialist returns operator-influenced content.


## Deferred from: code review of 2a-13-sdlc-ux-phase-2-ux-track review-B (2026-05-14)

- **WB1 — Diff-construction process gap.** `git diff <base>` does NOT include untracked files by default; review-A's diff to `/tmp/2a13-diff-rB.patch` initially excluded `_ux_pipeline.py` and `_boundary.py`. Blind-Hunter review-B flagged this as missing files. **Activation trigger:** before review-C, always run `git add -N` on new files before generating the review diff.
- **WB2 — macOS NFD/NFC filename collisions.** Specialist returns `01-café.md` (NFC) and `01-café.md` (NFD) — Python string equality treats them as distinct, but APFS normalises both to the same on-disk name. P4/PB8 duplicate-filename guard would not catch this. **Activation trigger:** when first cross-platform macOS test failure surfaces.
- **WB3 — TOCTOU between `target.exists()` and `target.read_text()` / `target.write_text()`.** Concurrent process can replace target with a symlink between checks. Same family as W6 (concurrent `run_ux` lockless). **Activation trigger:** framework-wide concurrency story (covers W6 + WB3).
- **WB4 — FIFO/socket/device-node as `01-PRODUCT.md` or as a UX target.** `is_file()` returns True for symlinks-to-files; `read_text` blocks on FIFO. No size cap or `O_NOFOLLOW` flag. **Activation trigger:** any incident report involving non-regular-file inputs.
- **WB5 — Filename byte-length cap interaction with NFD normalisation.** P9 caps at 100 bytes NFC; on-disk NFD representation may exceed if non-ASCII characters present. Currently impossible due to `re.ASCII` (PB7) forbidding non-ASCII, but if regex relaxed, this re-emerges.
- **WB6 — `json.loads` `RecursionError` not in except tuple** (`_ux_pipeline.py:189-195`). Hostile specialist response with 1000+ nested arrays triggers DoS-style RecursionError; caught only by outer generic `except Exception` → opaque `ERR_UX_DISPATCH_FAILED`. **Activation trigger:** add `RecursionError` to except tuple when adversarial-specialist testing lands.
- **WB7 — `pydantic.ValidationError` in `build_write_intent_payload`.** Embedded newlines in `rel` (from a maliciously-crafted symlink target leaked via `_relative_to_root`) → `HookPayload` validation fails. Currently propagates as generic `Exception`. **Activation trigger:** path-validation refactor.
- **WB8 — `agent_dispatched` written BEFORE dispatch succeeds** — already tracked as W1 (review-A). Re-affirmed by review-B; resolves only when atomic write-primitive lands (W2/EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE).
- **WB9 — `SDLC_USE_MOCK_RUNTIME` env-gate sibling pattern.** Siblings (`epics.py`, `stories.py`) gate mock-runtime via `_epics_pipeline.use_mock_runtime()`; UX unconditionally uses MockAIRuntime. Extended W3 (real runtime lands in Story 2B.9). **Activation trigger:** real-runtime wire-up.
- **WB10 — Naming asymmetry** `_epics_pipeline.dispatch_and_write` vs `_ux_pipeline.ux_dispatch_and_write_async`. Cosmetic but worth aligning in a future refactor pass.
- **WB11 — `_ux_pipeline.ux_dispatch_and_write_async` still carries `noqa: PLR0915`** (sibling `_epics_pipeline.dispatch_and_write` only needs `C901`). Indicates the function is 4+ statements heavier than sibling; refactor opportunity.
- **WB12 — `agents/phase2/__init__.py` not present.** Spec AC4 Task 1.1 said "if required by package structure". Currently `agents/` is treated as a resource directory not a Python package; verify package-data discovery still works on `pip install`.
- **WB13 — `epics.py:28` still imports `_artifact_contains_boundary` via `verify.py` re-export.** P13 promoted the helper to `_boundary.py`; `verify.py` keeps the alias for backward compat. A cleanup pass that removes the verify re-export would silently break `epics.py`. **Activation trigger:** before P13's cleanup follow-up — also update `epics.py` to import directly from `_boundary`.
- **WB14 — D3 manual rebase pending.** Commit `73abf94` still bundles spec + RED + GREEN + e2e + status flip into one commit. Per CONTRIBUTING.md §2 (TDD-first ordering visible in `git log --reverse`) this is a process gap. Resolves when user runs `git rebase -i 73abf94^` to split, OR when Epic 2A retro formally accepts as a one-time exception.
- **WB15 — `test_rejects_path_traversal_filename` + `test_rejects_non_md_filename` assert only `"ERR" in stdout+stderr`** — too loose; should assert specific `ERR_UNSAFE_FILENAME` code. Currently passes because the new code IS in the registry, but the test would also pass on `ERR_UX_DISPATCH_FAILED` or any other envelope. Defer; tighten in next refactor pass.

## Deferred from: code review of story-2a-14 (2026-05-17)

- **CR14-W1 — `dispatch_and_write` TOCTOU.** `content_hash_before` is snapshotted, passed to the hook chain, then `write_text` runs with no re-verification that the file still matches at write time. A concurrent mutation between snapshot and write is silently overwritten despite hook approval on stale state. [`_architect_pipeline.py:510-530`] — pre-existing dispatch infra; resolves with an atomic write primitive (cf. EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE).
- **CR14-W2 — `ARCHITECTURE.md` read with `utf-8` not `utf-8-sig`.** `01-PRODUCT.md` is read BOM-tolerant; `ARCHITECTURE.md` is read with plain `utf-8` in `parse_requires_block` and the sub-track loop. Safe today (framework writes the file, no BOM). **Activation trigger:** Story 2B.9 replaces the mock with a real model that may emit a BOM → `startswith("---")` fails → all sub-tracks silently dropped.
- **CR14-W3 — Sub-tracks dispatched with `postconditions=()`.** Each sub-track runs under an ad-hoc `WorkflowSpec` with no postconditions; an empty/missing `sub-tracks/*.md` is not caught by any postcondition, only by the `dispatch` outcome. Pairs with EPIC-2A-DEBT-POSTCONDITIONS — per-artifact postcondition wiring.
- **CR14-W4 — Concurrent runs can corrupt monotonic journal `seq`.** `allocate_seq` then `journal_append` are two non-atomic awaits with no file lock; two interleaving processes can allocate the same `seq`. [`_architect_pipeline.py:469,533`] — pre-existing journal infra.
- **CR14-W5 — `architecture_md_written` postcondition accepts a placeholder-only file.** The check only verifies `is_file()` + non-empty `text.strip()`; a file containing solely frontmatter or the literal `**PLACEHOLDER**` marker passes. [`postconditions.py:74-86`] — premature to tighten while the mock intentionally writes placeholder content; revisit with real generation in Story 2B.9.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-15-sdlc-bootstrap-phase-3-greenfield-scaffolding (2026-05-18)

- **CR15-W1 — tempfile TemporaryDirectory cleanup on Windows.** `MockAIRuntime` may hold open file handles into the TemporaryDirectory; cleanup on `__exit__` may fail with `PermissionError` on Windows. [`bootstrap.py:382-435`] — Windows-only; pre-existing mock infrastructure design.
- **CR15-W2 — Symlink traversal in `_source_exists` / `_check_source_root_populated`.** Both use `rglob("*")` which follows symlinks; cyclic symlink causes infinite loop; out-of-tree symlink satisfies "source exists" with non-project content. [`bootstrap.py:78`, `postconditions.py:361`] — adversarial scenario; use `os.walk(followlinks=False)` to harden.
- **CR15-W3 — Duplicate `_BOOTSTRAP_PLACEHOLDER_ALLOWLIST` without shared import.** Defined identically in `cli/bootstrap.py` and `dispatcher/postconditions.py`; cross-reference comment exists (D1 decision). Risk: one set updated without the other causes `_source_exists` / `source_root_populated` divergence. Consolidate into shared constants in a later story.
- **CR15-W4 — Mock fixture hash-key collision risk.** `_write_mock_fixture` keys the fixture by `compute_prompt_hash(mock_prompt)`; content change → hash change → MockAIRuntime finds no matching fixture. [`bootstrap.py:118-122`] — mock infrastructure design; acceptable for v1.
- **CR15-W5 — `noqa: C901, PLR0912, PLR0915` suppression on `run_bootstrap`.** Hides cyclomatic complexity; 15+ branches. Pre-existing pattern; address when extracting `_bootstrap_pipeline.py` (P1).
- **CR15-D1 — Hook denial mid-batch leaves partial writes with no rollback (EPIC-2A-DEBT-BOOTSTRAP-HOOK-PARTIAL-ROLLBACK).** If pre-write hook denies record N, files 0…N-1 remain on disk; next run auto-skips via `_source_exists`, masking the partial state. [`bootstrap.py:200-214`] — YAGNI for v1 MockAIRuntime; atomic write semantics deferred to Story 2B scope.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-16-sdlc-break-active-story-only-task-generation (2026-05-18)

- **CR16-W1 — Journal `artifact_written` entries not compensated on mid-batch rollback.** `break_dispatch_write` unlinks written task files on `WorkflowError`, but the `artifact_written` journal entries already appended for tasks 1…N-1 are left in place; a journal/filesystem-divergence consumer sees phantom artifacts. [`_break_pipeline.py:638`] — a compensating journal entry kind is out of Story 2A.16 scope.
- **CR16-W2 — `run_break` is a ~240-line function with `# noqa: C901,PLR0912,PLR0915`.** Exceeds the project 50-line guideline; the spec accepted the `_break_pipeline.py` split, so further decomposition is refactor debt. [`break_.py:run_break`]
- **CR16-W3 — Idempotency guard + rollback do not clean non-`T*-*.json` residue under `tasks/<STORY-id>/`.** Anchor/auxiliary files survive a failed run and are invisible to the `T*-*.json` glob guard, so they silently accumulate across re-runs. [`break_.py` Step 6 + `_break_pipeline.py` rollback]

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-17-sdlc-task-tdd-pipeline-5-stages (2026-05-18)

- **CR17-W1 — Rejected review is a dead-end.** A `code-reviewer` `rejected` verdict advances the task to `stage: review` (per AC5 "advances REGARDLESS of verdict"); the `review → done` transition then permanently refuses, and re-running `/sdlc-task` at `review` only re-checks the same stored verdict — there is no transition back to `write-code` for re-implementation. Behavior matches AC5/AC6 as written; recommend opening `EPIC-2A-DEBT-TASK-REJECTED-REWORK` to add a rejected→write-code rework path. [`_task_pipeline.py:398-412`]
- **CR17-W2 — Rollback deletes overwritten files; non-atomic task-JSON write.** AC7 rollback calls `p.unlink(missing_ok=True)` on written paths — if a specialist returned a path colliding with a pre-existing repo file, the stage `write_text`-clobbered it and rollback then deletes it (data loss, not restore). `task_path.write_text` is likewise non-atomic; a crash mid-write corrupts the task JSON so the next invocation cannot parse it. Folds under inherited `EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE`. [`_task_pipeline.py:417,443-445`]
- **CR17-W3 — Concurrent invocation race.** Two `/sdlc-task` invocations on the same TASK-id both read the same `stage`, both dispatch, both rewrite the task JSON and journal — double stage advance + duplicate artifact writes. No per-task lock. Inherited `EPIC-2A-DEBT-PANEL-V1-PROCESS-LOCAL-SEQ`; v1 single-user posture. [`task.py:run_task`]
- **CR17-W4 — `artifact_written` journal entries not compensated on rollback.** Stage files are journaled `artifact_written` per file inside the write loop; on a later failure the files are unlinked but the journal entries remain. Append-only journal — `task_stage_failed` is the compensation marker. Same posture as CR16-W1. [`_task_pipeline.py:367-387`]
- **CR17-W5 — Hook payload `content_hash_before=None` on overwrites.** Every stage file write builds `build_write_intent_payload(..., write_intent="create", content_hash_before=None)` even when the target already exists; a drift/tamper hook relying on the prior hash is blind to the overwrite. Fail-open hook posture inherited (`EPIC-2A-DEBT-CLAUDE-HOOK-FAIL-CLOSED-V1.X`). [`_task_pipeline.py:344-349`]

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-17-sdlc-task-tdd-pipeline-5-stages (2026-05-19)

- `ERR_PHASE2_NOT_APPROVED` / `ERR_TASK_STAGE_FAILED` are not registered in `cli/output.py:_ERR_CODE_TO_EXIT_CODE`; both fall through to `_DEFAULT_EXIT_CODE=1`. Pre-existing: `break_.py`/`bootstrap.py` (2A.15/2A.16) also emit unregistered `ERR_PHASE2_NOT_APPROVED`. Functionally non-zero (AC1/AC7 satisfied) and the map documents a historical fallback. Register these codes epic-wide as a batch.
- `_use_mock_runtime()` defaults mock-ON in production (`SDLC_USE_MOCK_RUNTIME` defaults to `"1"`) and the CLI surface emits no "output is a placeholder" notice — MockAIRuntime writes `assert False` test stubs + empty `# Implementation stub` source and the command exits 0 reporting success. Epic-wide v1 posture (real `ClaudeAIRuntime` lands in Epic 2B). Consider an epic-wide `mock: true` flag in success envelopes so callers can distinguish real vs placeholder output.
- Rollback in `task_stage_dispatch_write` unlinks written files but leaves newly-created parent directories (`tests/unit/`, `src/sdlc/`) on disk after a failed run. Same class as CR16-W3; folds under `EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE`.
- Task JSON is read with `utf-8-sig` (BOM-stripping) but the rollback path rewrites it with `utf-8` — a BOM-bearing original silently loses its BOM on restore, so AC7's "stage left UNCHANGED" file restore is not byte-identical. Theoretical: framework-written task JSON never carries a BOM.
- `cause`/exception-string truncation to 500 chars is applied only to the `ERR_SIGNOFF_READ_FAILED` path in `run_task`; every other `emit_error` call passes the full untruncated `str(exc)`. Cosmetic envelope-bloat inconsistency; normalize epic-wide.
- `_task_pipeline.py:287` accesses `result.agent_result.output_text` unguarded — an `AttributeError` results if `result.outcome=='success'` but `agent_result is None`. Low likelihood: the dispatch contract guarantees `agent_result` on a success outcome; add a defensive guard if the contract ever loosens.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-18-sdlc-next (2026-05-19)

- Circular / self task dependencies (`T1→T2`, `T2→T1`, or `T→T`) are silently treated as permanently "blocked by dependencies" with no diagnostic — `_deps_satisfied` (`_next_resolver.py:140-144`) only ever returns False for them. A malformed task graph is indistinguishable from a legitimately-blocked one. Upstream-validated by Story 2A.16's dep-DAG Kahn check, so defensive-only here; add a cycle-detection blocker reason if `/sdlc-next` ever consumes task graphs not produced by `/sdlc-break`.
- A dependency referencing a non-existent task ID (typo, deleted task) is counted in `blocked_by_deps` rather than surfaced as a distinct data-integrity error (`_next_resolver.py:142-143`). Upstream-validated by Story 2A.16 story-lineage cross-check; surface a `missing_dependency` blocker if upstream validation is ever bypassed.
- Two task JSON files deserializing to the same `_TaskEntry.id` silently overwrite each other in `all_tasks` (`_next_resolver.py:134`); dependency checks then resolve against the wrong task. Upstream-validated by Story 2A.16 task-ID uniqueness check; add a duplicate-id guard for defence-in-depth.
- An all-done task batch that also contains malformed (soft-skipped) task files still reports "all tasks complete" (`_next_resolver.py:161-174`) — `done_count == len(task_paths)` only counts parseable paths, so broken files are masked. `_load_task` soft-skip is a documented posture; consider surfacing an `unparsed_tasks` count in the `blockers` map.
- `_parse_story_seq` (`_next_resolver.py:106-109`) re-derives the story `seq` from the task directory name via `re.search(r"-S(\d{2})-", ...)` with `fallback=999`, ignoring `parse_story_id`. Any story ID whose seq segment is not exactly two hyphen-bracketed digits silently sorts last. Works for the canonical `EPIC-<slug>-S<NN>-<slug>` format; switch to `parse_story_id` when a parser is available.
- The integration `_invoke` helper (`test_sdlc_next.py:1043-1046`) patches only `sdlc.cli.next_._get_repo_root_or_cwd`, while the e2e `_invoke_next` dual-patches `sdlc.cli.task._get_repo_root_or_cwd` too. `run_task` is mocked in every current integration test so the gap is harmless now; any future integration test that lets a real dispatch through would resolve the repo root via `cwd` instead of `tmp_path`.
- `01-Requirement/01-PRODUCT.md` existing as a directory (or broken symlink) makes `is_file()` return False, so the resolver reports "phase 1 not started" and suggests `/sdlc-start` for what is actually a corrupt project state (`_next_resolver.py:188`). Exotic edge; add an explicit path-exists-but-not-file branch if corrupt-state diagnostics become a priority.
- `_stories_exist_for_epic` (`_next_resolver.py:82-87`) tests for story JSON presence via glob, not parseability — an epic whose `05-Stories/<epic_id>/` contains only corrupt JSON is treated as having stories, so the ladder skips it and advances to `/sdlc-signoff 1` with broken data. Upstream-validated at story-creation time.

## Deferred from: code review of 2a-19-sdlc-replan-mark-stale-invalidate-downstream (2026-05-19)

- **CR19-W1 — Partial-failure leaves an inconsistent audit chain.** `replan_invalidated` is journaled first (AC9, by design); if `invalidate_record` raises mid-loop for phase 2 after phase 1 succeeded — or a `signoff_invalidated` journal append fails after `invalidate_record` already mutated the YAML — the journal and on-disk signoff state disagree about which phases were invalidated, with no compensating entry or rollback. Fail-loud is spec-intended (AC9 line 138 / Dev Notes line 240); compensation/atomicity is a recurring deferred theme (cf. CR17-W2/W4, `EPIC-2A-DEBT-WRITE-PRIMITIVE`). [`src/sdlc/cli/replan_cmd.py:124-173`]
- **CR19-W2 — Trace global-event passthrough edge cases.** `_add_postdating_globals` anchors `earliest_task_ts` on the earliest of journal+agent-run events, but the docstring/AC6 header says "first journal entry"; a task with zero journal entries drops all globals; the `>=` comparison surfaces a replan sharing the task's exact millisecond timestamp. All low-impact on the spec-mandated AC6/D1 passthrough. [`src/sdlc/cli/trace.py:_add_postdating_globals`]
- **CR19-W3 — Hardcoded replan reason, no `--reason` option.** Every replan journals the identical `_DEFAULT_REASON = "invalidated by replan"`; the audit chain captures nothing about *why* the replan happened. The spec did not mandate a configurable reason — out of 2A.19 scope; consider a `--reason` CLI option. [`src/sdlc/cli/replan_cmd.py:34`]
- **CR19-W4 — `before_hash=None` + TOCTOU re-read for `signoff_invalidated.after_hash`.** The `signoff_invalidated` entry sets `before_hash=None` (pre-invalidation hash is trivially obtainable) and computes `after_hash` by re-reading the file from disk rather than hashing the `inv_record` that `invalidate_record` returned — a concurrent writer between write and re-read makes `after_hash` non-corresponding. Folds under inherited `EPIC-2A-DEBT-SIGNOFF-FLOCK-CONCURRENCY`. [`src/sdlc/cli/replan_cmd.py:147-164`]
- **CR19-W5 — Private cross-module imports.** `replan_cmd.py` imports `_signoff_path` and `_is_safe_repo_relative_posix` (underscore-private) from `signoff.records`; a refactor of those private names breaks `replan` with no contract test catching it. `_is_safe_repo_relative_posix` reuse was explicitly spec-sanctioned (AC1 line 24); `_signoff_path` was not. Promote to a public `sdlc.signoff` surface. [`src/sdlc/cli/replan_cmd.py:29,145`]
- **CR19-W6 — `noqa: C901` on `run_replan` masks complexity.** `trace.py` was refactored into `_partition_journal`/`_collect_agent_run_events` in this same diff, but `run_replan`'s complexity was suppressed rather than extracted — inconsistent treatment within one changeset. LOC budget (≤320) is met; refactor debt only. [`src/sdlc/cli/replan_cmd.py:37`]

## Deferred from: code review of 2b-1-claudeairuntime-implementation-subprocess-management (2026-05-22)

- **CR2B1-W1 — `asyncio.CancelledError` orphans the `claude` subprocess.** `ClaudeAIRuntime.dispatch` runs the blocking work via `await asyncio.to_thread(_invoke_claude_blocking, ...)`. If the awaiting coroutine is cancelled (outer `asyncio.wait_for`, panel timeout, Ctrl-C), the `await` raises `CancelledError` immediately but the worker thread cannot be cancelled — `_invoke_claude_blocking` keeps running and the `claude` child runs to its own 300 s timeout fully detached. AC4's "no orphans" only covers the internal timeout path; caller-side cancellation is unaddressed. Proper fix needs a cancellation bridge (expose the `proc` handle, kill on cancel) or the AC1/D2 `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec` approach the spec rejected. [`src/sdlc/runtime/claude.py:135`]
- **CR2B1-W2 — `mock` field absent from `dispatch_attempt` on failed/retry outcomes.** `_run_member` sets `attempt_payload["mock"]` only when `outcome == "success" and resolved_agent_result is not None`; a `dispatch_attempt` line for a failed/retried attempt carries no `mock` key, so the journal schema is non-uniform across attempts of one dispatch. The obvious fix — derive `mock` from `isinstance(runtime, MockAIRuntime)` — is explicitly rejected by ADR-029 §Alternatives (couples the dispatcher to runtime concrete types). On a failed attempt no `AgentResult` exists, so `mock` is genuinely unavailable without an ABC-boundary violation. [`src/sdlc/dispatcher/_panel_helpers.py:506-507`]
- **CR2B1-W3 — No `cwd` control on the `claude` subprocess.** `subprocess.Popen` is called without a `cwd=` argument, so the `claude` child inherits whatever working directory the `sdlc` process has. Combined with `del context`, a caller cannot scope the agent to a project root. Low impact in v1 (dispatch is prompt-in / `AgentResult`-out; the dispatcher writes the artifact, not `claude`); revisit when agent file-scoping becomes a requirement. [`src/sdlc/runtime/claude.py:85`]
- **CR2B1-W4 — Temp `fixtures_dir` created and passed to `ClaudeAIRuntime` unused.** Every dispatch CLI command wraps dispatch in `with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory()` and calls `build_runtime(fixtures_dir=tmp_path)`; `build_runtime` constructs `ClaudeAIRuntime()` ignoring `fixtures_dir`, so in the default real mode a temp dir is created and torn down for nothing under a parameter name that is a lie for the real path. Functionally harmless; a clean fix is a cross-cutting refactor across ~9 CLI modules. [`src/sdlc/cli/_runtime_selection.py:71`]
- **CR2B1-W5 — Brittle coupling to `claude --output-format json`.** `_invoke_claude_blocking` hard-codes `["claude", "-p", "--output-format", "json"]` and `_parse_claude_stdout` assumes a single top-level JSON object. A `claude` version (or wrapper) emitting `stream-json` NDJSON makes `json.loads` raise → "malformed JSON". No `--output-format` capability check or version guard. Mitigated by Story 2B.2 pinning a Claude Code minimum version. [`src/sdlc/runtime/claude.py:83`]
- **CR2B1-W6 — `--json` command output carries no mock-mode signal.** When `--json` is set, `enforce_allow_mock_gate` correctly suppresses the stderr WARN, but nothing is added to the command's JSON envelope — a machine consumer running `SDLC_USE_MOCK_RUNTIME=1 --allow-mock --json` receives a normal-looking success envelope; the only mock signal is `payload.mock` / `allow_mock_invoked` in the journal. ADR-029 routes the signal via journal + dashboard, so this is an enhancement, not a spec gap. [`src/sdlc/cli/_runtime_selection.py:51-53`]
- **CR2B1-W7 — P16 test-infra residual: narrow the autouse mock fixture + add real-runtime CLI coverage.** Story 2B.1 review P16 replaced the production `_pytest_active()` gate-bypass with the explicit `SDLC_MOCK_GATE_BYPASS` env opt-in, but two larger test-infrastructure changes remain: (1) the root `tests/conftest.py` `autouse` fixture still forces `SDLC_USE_MOCK_RUNTIME=1` for the *entire* suite — narrowing it to per-area conftests (`tests/unit/cli`, `tests/integration`, `tests/e2e`) needs a full-suite shake-out of tests that implicitly depend on mock-on; (2) no CLI-level test exercises `build_runtime` → real `ClaudeAIRuntime` end-to-end (a stub `claude` on PATH driven through a `sdlc` command), which is the coverage gap that let the P1 CRITICAL regression hide from CI. Unit-level real-runtime coverage exists (`test_dispatch_happy_path_stub_claude`, `test_build_runtime_selects_claude_when_mock_off`); the CLI-level gap is the residual. [`tests/conftest.py:16-21`]

## Deferred from: code review of 2b-4-prompt-injection-corpus-ci-regression (2026-05-27)

- **CR2B4-W1 — `idea_text in prompt` verbatim brittleness.** `_assert_boundary_before_user_idea` asserts `idea_text in prompt` as a plain substring. Current corpus payloads don't trip whitespace/encoding normalization mismatch, but a future builder that re-wraps or normalizes whitespace breaks the assertion silently. Tighten to envelope-bracketed form (`f"<USER_IDEA>\n{idea_text}\n</USER_IDEA>" in prompt`) when a concrete fixture exposes it; current shape is documented as known-loose. [`tests/security/test_prompt_injection_corpus.py:~120`]
- **CR2B4-W2 — CRLF / newline normalization.** Corpus `read_text + splitlines + "\n".join` collapses CRLF→LF; framework is POSIX-only v1 so no Windows-test regression today. Add `.gitattributes` rule `tests/security/corpus/** text eol=lf` when Windows contributors emerge or when a fixture deliberately tests CR-only injection. [`tests/security/corpus/`]
- **CR2B4-W3 — EPIC-2B-DEBT-DASH-CATEGORY (production-code edge).** `_DASH_VARIANTS` in `src/sdlc/dispatcher/prompts.py:40-47` only folds 6 specific Unicode dashes; full Unicode `Pd` general category and `Sm` minus signs (U+2212 MINUS SIGN, U+FE63 SMALL HYPHEN-MINUS, U+FF0D FULLWIDTH HYPHEN-MINUS) bypass `normalize_for_boundary_check` detection. Story 2B.4 is test-only; promote to production-hardening debt-budget row. Owner: Epic 2B follow-up or `EPIC-2B-DEBT-DASH-CATEGORY` against `prompts.py`.
- **CR2B4-W4 — EPIC-2B-DEBT-SPECIALIST-BODY-BOUNDARY-NORMALIZE (production-code edge).** `BOUNDARY_LINE in specialist.body` at `src/sdlc/dispatcher/prompts.py:232` (and `:313` for compound builder) uses raw substring rather than `normalize_for_boundary_check`. Specialist body sits inside trust boundary (only specialist `.md` files in the repo), so impact is low — but a compromised specialist file could smuggle `＝＝＝ USER-PROVIDED DATA — NOT INSTRUCTIONS ＝＝＝` (NFKC-fullwidth) past the check. Owner: production-hardening sprint.
- **CR2B4-W5 — EPIC-2B-DEBT-CORPUS-LOAD-REAL-SPEC.** Hand-rolled `_sdlc_start_spec()` + `_product_strategist()` (lines 79-109) in the harness construct a `WorkflowSpec`/`Specialist` via direct constructor with hard-coded paths, agent names, and frontmatter fields. A schema change in `WorkflowSpec` (e.g., new required field, contract evolution per ADR-024/-025) breaks the harness at import. Also: `parallel_agents=("technical-researcher", "devil-advocate")` declared without entries in `write_globs` may itself be invalid by `static_check.validate_workflow` standards (currently masked because `phase1_prompt_builder` does not invoke `validate_workflow`). Refactor: load real Phase-1 spec from disk via `WorkflowRegistry.load("/sdlc-start")` or read a fixture YAML through `load_workflow`. Significant work; deferred to follow-up. [`tests/security/test_prompt_injection_corpus.py:~79-109`]
- **CR2B4-W6 — 2B.5 reverse cross-reference handshake.** 2B.4 cross-references 2B.5 (`tests/security/test_boundary_line_presence.py`) in `README.md` §"Template census" and harness docstring; 2B.5 must add the reciprocal reference before either Layer-1 sibling merges. AC3/D2 mandates "Cross-reference both directions". 2B.4 cannot close this alone — pre-merge handshake item.
- **CR2B4-W7 — Production glob-overlap detector smoke test.** `static_intra_agent_glob_overlap.yaml`, `static_disjoint_writes_overlap.yaml` use `**` segments assuming `pathspec`/`gitignore`-style globbing; if the production detector (`src/sdlc/workflows/static_check.py:208-321`) uses shell `fnmatch`, `**` does NOT match nested directories — and these fixtures would silently fail to overlap. Smoke test of the detector against known overlap/disjoint inputs is out of 2B.4 scope; track for production hardening.
- **CR2B4-W8 — `spec` binding leaked outside `with pytest.raises` block.** `_assert_workflow_corpus_rejected`: `with pytest.raises(WorkflowError): spec = load_workflow(path); validate_workflow(spec)`. The `spec` variable is bound only if `load_workflow` succeeds; subsequent code touching `spec` would `UnboundLocalError`. Cosmetic Python pitfall; restructure when D2 split lands. [`tests/security/test_prompt_injection_corpus.py:~133-139`]
- **CR2B4-W9 — `Specialist(source_path=Path(__file__))` lies about provenance.** Test fixture's `_product_strategist()` passes `source_path=Path(__file__)` — claims provenance from the test file. No current downstream consumer dereferences `source_path` in a way that affects test outcomes, but future helpers using `source_path` for relative-path resolution would silently get test-file paths instead of agent-md paths. Cosmetic / future footgun. [`tests/security/test_prompt_injection_corpus.py:~104`]

The violation is still flagged — the citation is just imprecise. Hardening alongside P12: AST-walk to the actual user-text statement node and use its `lineno`. ## Deferred from: code review of 2b-3-behavioral-conformance-mock-vs-claude (2026-05-28)

- **CR2B3-W1 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-PHASE-GATE-DISCOVERY-COUPLING** — `bound_phase_gate.__is_phase_gate__ = True` magic attribute attached to a `functools.partial` object inside the conformance hook-chain helper. Production hook-runner discovery may inspect this attribute; the test piggybacks on undocumented coupling. Hardening: add a unit test pinning the production attribute contract OR refactor to a typed hook wrapper class. [`tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:165-171`]
- **CR2B3-W2 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-PRODUCTION-HOOK-CHAIN-PINNING** — `build_conformance_hook_chain` returns `(naming_validator, bound_phase_gate)` "mirroring dispatcher wiring without importing dispatcher/." If production adds a third hook or reorders, mock-vs-claude byte-identity remains green while the dispatcher's actual emission diverges. Hardening: introduce a snapshot/property test that imports the dispatcher's real chain tuple and asserts conformance helper equals it. [`tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:161-171`]
- **CR2B3-W3 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-STUB-NOEXEC-FALLBACK** — Stub installation does `chmod 0o755` then `subprocess.Popen(["claude", ...])`. On noexec-mounted `/tmp` (some CI containers / sandboxed FS), Popen raises `PermissionError` and the failure surfaces as opaque `DispatchError(stage="spawn")`. Hardening: detect noexec at install time and fall back to `subprocess.Popen([sys.executable, str(stub_path), ...])`. [`tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:230, 313`]
- **CR2B3-W4 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-STUB-ENV-SCRUB** — `install_claude_stub_on_path` prepends bindir to PATH but does NOT scrub `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `CLAUDE_BIN`, or other env that would let `claude` reach a real backend if the stub falls back. Hardening: `monkeypatch.delenv("ANTHROPIC_API_KEY", raising=False)` etc. in `_claude_factory`. [`tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:300-313`]
- **CR2B3-W5 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-STUB-EXTRACT-TO-FILE** — Stub script is generated via `textwrap.dedent` + f-string with `{{`/`}}` escapes. Double-escape bugs are a future maintainer hazard. Hardening: extract to standalone `tests/integration/_stubs/claude_stub_template.py` and copy via `shutil.copy2`. [`tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:240-285`]
- **CR2B3-W6 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-STUB-PROMPT-CONTRACT** — Stub assumes `ClaudeAIRuntime.dispatch` writes `_SEED_PROMPT` to stdin verbatim with no decoration. Future `ClaudeAIRuntime` changes (argv-passing, system-prompt prepending) silently break conformance. Hardening: document the stdin protocol as an invariant of `runtime/claude.py` and pin via a runtime unit test. [`tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:209-210, src/sdlc/runtime/claude.py`]
- **CR2B3-W7 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-HOOK-NAME-RENAME-AUDIT** — Golden change `target_kind: "epic" → "write_intent"` and `hook_name: "abstraction-adequacy-synth" → "pre_write"`. Audit downstream taxonomies (ADR-028 §3, dashboard taxonomy in Epic 5) for orphaned references to the old strings. [`tests/fixtures/abstraction_adequacy/expected_hook_payloads.json:55`]
- **CR2B3-W8 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-PRETTY-PRINT-DIFF** — `_format_diff` for single-line JSON state shows mega-line `-{...}` vs `+{...}` unified diffs that are unreadable in CI logs. Hardening: pretty-print via `json.dumps(parsed, indent=2, sort_keys=True)` round-trip before splitting for diffing. [`tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:93-103`]
- **CR2B3-W9 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-RECURSIVE-CANONICAL-JSON** — `json.dumps(..., sort_keys=True)` sorts only top-level; nested dict insertion order persists. HookPayload v1 has no nested dicts so currently safe; future fields could silently break mock-vs-claude byte-identity. Hardening: introduce a `canonical_json(obj)` helper that recursively sorts dict keys at every depth, use it wherever conformance bytes are produced. [`tests/integration/test_abstraction_adequacy.py:166-174`]
- **CR2B3-W10 — TDD-first commit ordering enforcement at merge time** — All 2B.3 changes are currently uncommitted (`git status` shows M/?? on the relevant paths). Per CONTRIBUTING §2 + ADR-026 §2 squash-flow, the public test surface (parametrised `runtime` fixture extension + AC2/D2 cross-run assertion) must show RED-before-GREEN in `git log --reverse`. Reviewer must require split commits before merge: (1) RED with parametrised fixture + cross-run assertion only, (2) GREEN with stub-derivation and helper. [git history]
- **CR2B3-W11 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-PROJECTION-MOCK-STRIP-NARROW** — Projection's `mock`-strip filter applies to every `state_mutation` entry regardless of `payload.source` discriminator. If a future story emits `mock` as a legitimate domain field (not the ADR-029 audit-trail marker), it gets silently dropped from `state.json`. Hardening: gate the strip on a payload-source discriminator OR document the constraint via inline comment + a scanning unit test. [`src/sdlc/state/projection.py:91-96`]
- **CR2B3-W12 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-CLAUDE-TOOL-CALLS** — `ClaudeAIRuntime._parse_claude_stdout` returns `tool_calls=()` unconditionally; `_build_pre_chain_input_payload` papers over with `_SEED_TARGET_PATH` + `_ZERO_HASH` fallback. Mock-vs-Claude HookPayload identity holds only by coincidence (seed YAML happens to encode those exact values). v1 accepts this — see the `COINCIDENCE-COUPLING (CR2B3-W12)` comment block at the fallback site, pinned by `test_seed_fixture_tool_call_matches_conformance_fallback_constants` (any seed edit changing target/hash goes RED). Hardening: extend `runtime/claude.py:_parse_claude_stdout` to parse `tool_calls` from JSON envelope's `result` field; drop fallback; conformance becomes a real measurement. **Owner:** 2B.10 specialist-authoring layer (first specialist that actually emits tool_calls forces this). [`src/sdlc/runtime/claude.py:_parse_claude_stdout`, `tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:152-156`]
- **CR2B3-W13 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-CHAIN-EMISSION-CAPTURE** — `run_hook_chain` is invoked for `decision == "allow"` side-effect only; the goldens compare what the helper synthesised, NOT what the chain emitted. AC1/D2 D1 wording ("the dispatched chain emits HookPayloads — capture the emission order") is partially honoured via the decision invariant. Hardening: extend `hooks.runner` to expose emission list (or pass a recording sink); capture in test; assert goldens against emissions. **Owner:** 2B.10 specialist-authoring layer (when Phase-3 specialists land, chain emissions become richer and the decision-only invariant no longer suffices). [`src/sdlc/hooks/runner.py`, `tests/integration/_abstraction_adequacy_helpers.py:217-236`]

## Deferred from: story 2b-7-docs-threat-model-ai-native-risk-profile (2026-05-29)

- **EPIC-2B-DEBT-SPECIALIST-FILE-INTEGRITY** — No content-digest or cryptographic-hash verification of specialist `.md` files exists in v1. The specialist directory (`src/sdlc/specialists/`) contains `validator.py`, `frontmatter.py`, `manifest.py`, `registry.py`, and `__init__.py` — none of which compute or verify a SHA-256 digest of the specialist body before dispatch. A tampered or supply-chain-compromised specialist file that avoids corpus-covered patterns and does not trigger the destructive-op classifier (`src/sdlc/dispatcher/safety.py`) would be dispatched to Claude without detection. **Dominant residual risk for SDLC-THREAT-005** (see `docs/threat-model.md`). Hardening: at `sdlc init` / `sdlc trust-hooks` time, compute SHA-256 digests of all specialist `.md` files under `src/sdlc/agents/` and store the baseline (analogous to hook-trust detection in `src/sdlc/hooks/tampering.py`); verify digests before each dispatch; expose via `sdlc hook-check` or a new `sdlc verify-specialists` sub-command. Cross-references: **W12** (`_bmad-output/implementation-artifacts/deferred-work.md` — `idea_hash` threat-model documentation, Epic 2B security threat-model docs); **CR2B6-W10** (lazy nonce generation, `src/sdlc/dispatcher/_panel_helpers.py:442`); **CR2B5-W4 / EPIC-2B-DEBT-BOUNDARY-LINE-PRE-COMMIT-WIRE** (boundary-line presence not wired to pre-commit; same DX-hardening category). **Owner:** post-2B.7 dedicated specialist-integrity story or Epic 3. [`src/sdlc/specialists/`, `src/sdlc/hooks/tampering.py`, `docs/threat-model.md`]
